<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">509<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Ulrich von Hutten </i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[1488 â€“ 1523]<b>,</b> "<b>Knight of the Order of
Poets</b>"<b>, by David Starr Jordan</b>, President of Leland Stanford Jr.
University, "Die Luft der Freibeit Webt", Boston, American Unitarian
Association, 25 Beacon Street, "<b>1910</b>".<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>PREFATORY NOTE<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>For many of the details of the
life of Hutten, and for most of the quotations from Hutten's writings given in
this book, the writer is indebted to the excellent memoir by David Friedrich
Strauss, entitled</b> "<b>Ulrich von Hutten.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>(Fourth Edition:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Bonn, 1878.)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>No attempt
has been made to give here an account of <b>Hutten</b>'s writings, only a few
of the more noteworthy being mentioned.'<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'....<b>The death of Hutten was,
after all, not untimely.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He had
done his work.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His was the "voice
of one crying in the wilderness."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The head of <b>John the Baptist</b> lay on the charger before <b>Jesus</b>
had fulfilled his mission [some Christian mythology].<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Arnold Winkelried</b>, at Sempach, filled his body with
Austrian spears before the Austrian phalanx was broken.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>John Brown</b> <b>fell at Harper's Ferry</b>
before a blow was struck against slavery.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Ulrich von Hutten</b> had set every man, woman and child in Germany
to thinking of his relations to the Lord and to the Pope.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His mission was completed; and longer life
for him, as <b>Strauss </b>has suggested, might have led to discord among the <b>Reformers</b>
themselves.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>For this lover of freedom</b>
[Hutten] <b>was intolerant of intolerance.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>For fine points of doctrine he had only contempt.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>When the <b>Lutherans</b> began to treat as
enemies all <b>Reformers</b> who did not with them subscribe to the Confession
of Augsburg, <b>Hutten</b>'s fiery pen would have repudiated this
confession.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>For he</b> [Hutten] <b>fought
for freedom of the spirit, not for the Lutheran confession.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Had he remained in Switzerland, he
would have been still less in harmony with the prevailing conditions.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Not long after, <b>Zwingli</b> was slain in
the wretched battle of Kappel, and, after him, the <b>Swiss Reformation </b>passed
under the control of <b>John Calvin</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>There can be no doubt that the stern pietist [<b>Calvin</b>] of Geneva
would have burned <b>Ulrich von Hutten</b> with as calm a conscience as he did <b>Michael
Servetus</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The idea of a united and uniform
Church, whether Catholic, Lutheran, or Calvinist, had little attraction for
Hutten. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">510<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">He [<b>HUTTEN</b>]
<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">was one of the first to realize that
religion is individual, not collective.</span></b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">It is
concerned with life, not with creeds or ceremonies.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">In
the high sense, <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">no man can follow or share the religion of
another.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His religion, whatever it may
be, is his own. </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">It is
built up from his own thoughts and prayers and actions.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is the expression of his own ideals.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Only forms can be transferred unchanged
from man to man, from generation to generation</b>,â€”never realities.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For whatever is real to a man becomes part
of him, and partakes of his growth, and is modified by his personality.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten was buried where he died,
on the little island of Ufnau, in the Lake of Zurich, at the foot of the mighty
Alps.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>And some of his old associates
put over his grave a commemorative stone.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Afterwards, <b>the monks of the abbey of Einsiedeln, in Schwytz, came to
the island and removed the stone, and obliterated all traces of the grave.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>It was well that they did so; for
now the whole green island of Ufnau is his alone, and it is his worthy
sepulcher.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[40-42] [end of booklet].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">_____<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span>_____<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>_____<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">511<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Ulrich von Hutten </i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[1488 â€“ 1523]<b><i> and the German Reformation</i>,
by Hajo Holborn</b>, translated by <b>Roland H. Bainton</b>, Yale University
Press, <b>1937</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>Behind
the polemical writings composed in Italy against the Papacy and scholasticism,
beyond the <i>Epigrams to Crotus </i>and the <i>Letters of Obscure Men </i></b>[1515
â€“ 1517]<b>, was</b> a man [<b>Ulrich von Hutten</b>] who expected by his words
to incite deeds, because every intellectual apprehension carried with it a
direct practical command.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He, too, knew
the art of political concession.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For a
while he could watch and wait whether Fortune would give her wheel a favorable
turn, but he could not stay long in ambush.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>His ideas would start to ferment before he could make correct
observations.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was impelled in part
by a youthful swagger desirous of dazzling men by his recklessness, but this is
not the whole explanation.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He had
rather a superb and astounding contempt for obstacles and would have arrived
somewhere had he first come to grips with reality.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>His publication gives one the impression of native power of will
and conscience, yet contemptuous and even oblivious of the actual state of
affairs, as we have already indicated.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In the knightly romanticism, with which during his formative period he
invested and quickened the humanism of <b>Erasmus</b> and of German patriotism,
we see something of <b>the incapacity of medieval culture to face squarely the
hard facts of life.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Its Utopian
aspirations overlooked the devil, who, in spite of all exorcism, insinuated
himself into every spiritual endeavor.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The
life of the knight from which Hutton came</b>, from which he was never
emancipated, offers examples in abundance.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Eck later denounced Hutten before
the Curia precisely on account of his Italian epigrams,</b><sup>15</sup> <b>and
the Curia did well to be on its guard against the author of these incendiary
utterances.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In comparison with <b>Luther</b>,
who soon was to attract all eyes, <b>Hutten</b>'s writings seemed calculated to
disintegrate the Roman hierarchical system of the Middle Ages but not to bowl
it over.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The spiritual residue of his
pilgrimages was not comprehensive or potent enough to demolish the structure of
centuries.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It remained to be seen how
far during the struggle he would become aware of this, how far he would have
the power to seek deeper spiritual sources.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>At any rate, a more aggressive tone
was acquired through acquaintance with the exposure by <b>Lorenzo Valla </b>[c.
1406 â€“ 1457]<b> of the forged Donation of Constantine</b>, which <b>Hutten</b>,
on the point of returning to Germany, found at the house of <b>Cochlaeus</b>.<sup>16</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Ulrich</b> at once resolved to put out in
Germany a new imprint of this Italian who so excelled his time in critical
acumen and enlightenment.<sup>17</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>But something else, too, is recorded of <b>Hutten's last days in Italy.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He might have taken ship from Venice with
some cousins on a pilgrimage to the <b>Holy Land</b> had not <b>Crotus</b>
laughed him out of it.<sup>18</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>There could not be a <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">512<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">better
illustration of the dichotomy of his spiritual personality.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Who can fail to see how far the ideals of
medieval piety and the ideals of a universal world order continued to influence</b>
him [<b>Hutten</b>]?<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The second Italian period was
likewise disturbed and in a measure insecure.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In <b>Rome</b> he had a severe attack of that frightful disease
[syphilis] which he had sought in vain to cure before leaving for Italy.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>He [<b>Hutten</b>] wanted to go to
the <b>baths of Tuscany</b>, but in <b>Viterbo</b> he had a serious
mishap.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In a quarrel with several
Frenchmen he killed one of them...."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[80-81].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">_____<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;
</span>_____<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>_____<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>The Humanist Ulrich von Hutten</i>, A
Reappraisal of his Humor, Thomas W. Best</span></b><span style="font-family:
Arial">, The University of North Carolina Press, 1969.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>INTRODUCTION<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The humor</b><sup>1</sup> <b>of
the humanistic knight Ulrich von Hutten</b> (1488â€“1523)<b>, who was one of the
most satirical members of one of Germany's most satirical generations</b>, has
not been given adequate, accurate consideration.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten</b> has had great appeal in the past two-hundred years
for students of the <b>German</b> <b>Renaissance and Reformation</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was an intriguing and pathetic figure, a
tragic <b>Don Quixote</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He has been
one of Germany's most ardent patriots, admired by his country's nationalists
from <b>Herder</b>'s day to <b>Hitler</b>'s.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>If he failed to alter the course of the political history of his nation,
he did influence the development of its literature.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>For these reasons, and because his complete works have been
easily accessible in an excellent edition,<sup>2</sup> he has received a great
deal of scholarly attention, but almost none of this attention has been
concerned with his humor.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Albert
Bauer</b> has attempted to analyze <b>Hutten</b>'s satire in comparison to <b>Lucian</b>'s,
but his discussion of the subject is imprecise,<sup>3</sup> and those few who
have broached the larger matter of <b>Hutten</b>'s handling of the comic in
general have contented themselves with a glib sentence or two, usually basing
their remarks on his supposed contributions to the well-known satirical work of
the day, the <b><i>Epistolae obscurorum virorum</i></b> [<i>Letters of Obscure
Men</i>, 1515 â€“ 1517] (to be referred to subsequently in this study as the <i>Eov</i>).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>As we shall see, many of the letters in this
satire which have been ascribed to <b>Hutten</b> may not have been written by
him at all, making even more questionable those pronouncements on his humor
which were promulgated largely in connection with the <i>Eov</i>."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[1].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">513<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">"Since <b>Benzing</b> sets as a <i>terminus a
quo</i> ["earliest limiting point" ("a starting point or
origin")] for the publication of <b>Hutten</b>'s edition of <b><i>De
donatione Constantini</i> </b>September 1518,<sup>20</sup> the work must have
appeared in the autumn of the same year, so that a composition date for the
preface of December 1, 1517, is not at all unlikely.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Until stronger evidence is presented against it, the original
date must stand.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This date strengthens
the likelihood of sincerity in the preface by placing it in the period of <b>Hutten</b>'s
entrance into service with the archbishop of Mainz, at the time when <b>Hutten</b>
was otherwise writing very positively of <b>Leo</b>, as well.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Instead of supporting the
generally accepted thesis that </b>he<b> </b>[<b>Hutten</b>]<b> very early
became a bitter foe of Leo X, the available evidence indicates rather that
Hutten did not do so before the middle of 1519.</b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>How conclusive we find much of this evidence depends, to be sure,
on how willing we are to take him at his word, but the burden of proof lies
with those who are not willing to do so.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>At any rate, since it is questionable that <b>Hutten</b> wrote the
preface to his edition of <b><i>De donatione Constantini</i> </b>as irony, the
work should not be used to document any view of his satire."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[82] [end of text].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:

mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

â€“ 1999], Harvard University Press, <b>1963</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun:

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>INTRODUCTION</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>["1"]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Erasmus, the prince of the
humanists, presided regally over the German humanists</b>, but he himself
carried the ecclesiastical and religious humanist reform program to its fullest
development.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The question naturally
arises as to whether the religious thought of the <b>German humanists</b> was
Erasmian in a derivative or an analogous sense.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>To do Erasmus justice</b> requires digesting mountains of
scholarly material on him and epitomizing briefly the results of thousands of
monograph pages, in addition to analyzing his own tremendous works.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His position in humanism and toward the <b>Reformation</b>
cut across nearly all the problems in which the lesser humanists were
involved.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">Luther was not fond of Erasmus personally.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">He is as slippery as an eel,</span></b>"
he once commented, "<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">only Christ
can catch him.</span></b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[outstanding comment by Luther] [see 444, 458] <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">But
even after their famous exchange, <b>Luther</b> had such a high regard for the
mind of <b>Erasmus</b> that he continued to read his works.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His <i>philosophia Christi</i> is an
excellent summary of some of the major ingredients of the humanists' religious
thought and ecclesiastical reform programs.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The question of <b>Luther</b> and
humanism is a microcosm of the larger question of the relation of the <b>Reformation</b>
to the <b>Renaissance</b> which has agitated thinkers from <b>Nietzsche</b> and
<b>Troeltsch</b> down to the present time.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Luther</b> becomes, then, the essential terminal point for this study
of representative figures of the high generation of <b>German humanism</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His own association with the humanists and
with their cause and conversely their identification with his involves the
larger problem of the validity of Christian humanism in the light of the new
evangelical insight.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>It is now time to meet the
leading German humanists in person</b>....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[19].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">515<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>VI<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">HUTTEN </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[Ulrich
von Hutten 1488 â€“ 1523]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Militant Critic<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The year <b>1521</b> was tense with
crisis.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>All eyes were turned toward the
<b>Diet at Worms</b> where <b>Luther</b> [1483 â€“ 1546] made his courageous
stand in what <b>J.A. Froude</b> [see 367] described as "perhaps the
finest scene in human history."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Germany was alive with excitement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Above the tumult rose a persistent, strident voice, heard often before,
but soon to be hard no moreâ€”the voice of <b>Ulrich von Hutten, German</b> <b>knight</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He had called to <b>Luther</b>:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Long live liberty!"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Now the die was cast.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten</b> would not turn back, though
church and empire conspired to crush him.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>That year he [<b>Hutten</b>] <b>penned these words:</b><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>With open eyes I've dared it<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>And do not feel regret.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Though I should fail to conquer<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>True faith is with me yet.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Here indeed was a romantic figure [<b>Ulrich
von Hutten</b>] raised on the shoulders of <b>Uhland, Herder, Wieland,</b> and <b>Goethe</b>
to the stature of a national hero!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Freedom was all to this tempestuous, restless, daring young manâ€”free learning,
free Fatherland.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The weapons he chose
for battle were sword and pen.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Mutian</b>
characterized him as "sharp and vehement and a great poet, but such that
he can be irritated by the slightest word."<sup>1</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>["110"].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>Hutten</b>
was committed emotionally to <b>Luther</b>'s cause without ever really
understanding its essence.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>On April 17,
1521, <b>Hutten wrote to</b> "<b>the most invincible friend of the gospel</b>"
to fight strenuously for Christ, and not to give way to evils, but to go
against them more daringly.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b>
<b>thanked him for the letter</b>, and on April 20, <b>Hutten</b> wrote a
second letter declaring his faith that <b>Luther</b> would remain <b>Luther</b>.<sup>70</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten wrote to Pirckheimer</b>
describing the unfairness of the trial at Worms, where <b>Luther</b> was given
only one choice.<sup>71</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But for
all his enthusiasm for the reformer, <b>Hutten</b> remained vaguely aware of
the difference between them.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>In the first of the letters which <b>Hutten</b>
wrote to <b>Luther</b> during the opening session of the Diet of Worms, he gave
the classic expression to this difference:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"<b>We have, to be sure, different thoughts, for mine are human,
but you, more perfect, already live entirely for things divine.</b>"<sup>72</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten</b> felt that in a certain sense
he never was a Lutheran at all.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the <i>Expostulatio</i>
<b>Hutten</b> explained that, <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">516<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">though
he considered himself an independent, free of party affiliation, he allowed
himself to be called a Lutheran on the strength of the fact that he fought the
Roman tyranny.<sup>73</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>I
admire Luther's spirit,</b>" he wrote, "<b>and his incomparable power
in interpreting the secrets of Scripture, but Luther has been neither my
teacher nor my comrade.</b>"<sup>74</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>It was symbolic that <b>Hutten</b> rode off to join <b>Sickingen</b> and
not <b>Luther</b> in his war against tyranny.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Luther appreciated Hutten's
writings</b> in his behalf and his poems which were not calculated to please
Babylon.<sup>75</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But <b>Luther
could not condone Hutten's appeal to the sword as the final argument. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>On January 16, 1521, <b>Luther wrote to
Spalatin:</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"You see what <b>Hutten</b>
wishes.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But I do not desire to do
battle for the gospel with violence and murder and I wrote him as much.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Through the power of the Word the world is
conquered, through the power of the Word the church has been createdâ€”and
through the Word it will also be restored."<sup>76</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus</b> was all too right when in his
<i>Spongia</i> he sneered that some Lutherans, like <b>Hutten</b>, had nothing
of <b>Luther</b> about them except that they <b>maligned the Roman pontiff</b>.<sup>77</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hutten stood primarily for the outward
freedom of the German man rather than like Luther for the inner liberty of the
Christian man. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>His was the liberty
for which <b>Arminius</b> fought, freedom from the new Roman imperium.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Yet to his final days <b>Hutten</b>
acclaimed <b>Luther</b> a hero of the Word, a prophet who gathers a following
of the best men, a priest who is one with the Word he preaches.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[124-125].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>"<b>Hutten was basically a
romantic, imperialist, political propagandist, not a rationalistic liberal
humanist.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His social thinking was
contained entirely with traditional concepts of the <i>corpus christianum</i>,
and his basic criticisms of the church stemmed from his belief that the Curia
and its minions had encroached on the Emperor's prerogatives and those of his
imperial knights and had violated the ancient liberties of the empire.<sup>89</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He conceived his historical mission to be
the restoration of the right order of things.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Seeing <b>Hutten</b> in this light resolves many perplexing problems
with regard to his ambiguous relation to <b>humanism</b> and the <b>Reformation</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>For <b>Hutten</b> the belles-lettres
even of the classic authors were not an end in themselves.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Rather they were an instrument for the
cultural and political rejuvenation of the empire....<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>As a militant critic <b>Hutten</b>
was a pioneer and ally of the <b>Reformation</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>If the now-dated view of the <b>Reformation</b> as primarily an
attack on ecclesiastical abuses still prevailed, <b>Hutten</b> would rightly be
considered one of the <b>reformers</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>But <b>Hutten</b> did not understand the basic religious impulse of <b>Luther</b>'s
movement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To him the <b>Reformation</b>
was but an ally in a program dictated by his own class <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">517<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">status
and personal bent.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This is why he did
not view with alarm the overshadowing of the <b>renaissance</b> of learning by
the revival in religion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For him both
movements served the same end.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>A
controversial figure in a polemical age, he demonstrated to perfection that the
conservative and traditionalist when he assumes the offensive may upset the
world more than the self-conscious radical.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>How ironic that in the end he [<b>Hutten</b>]
was driven from the very empire for which he had dared all!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Befriended by <b>Zwingli</b>, he sought
refuge on the island of Ufenau in Lake Zurich.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>There he died in August 1523, of the same dread disease which had
claimed the life of his foe, <b>Julius II</b>, the <u>Aztec's revenge</u>
[here, <b>syphilis</b> [see 770-771].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The origin(s) of syphilis is much discussed.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">A common ailment, to the present, "<u>Montezuma's
revenge</u>", a miserable form of diarrhea, with which my body has had
personal experiences: <span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>in Mexico City;
Guanajuato; Mulege, and, Tijuana, Baja California; and, far reaching, from a
fruit stand just yards below the famous statue of Christ (Cristo Redentor),
Corcovado, Rio de Janeiro, Brazil (papaya juice!<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Some would consider that near medical emergency
experienceâ€”Christ's Revenge!).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
other severe miseries, I have forgotten].<sup>90</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">He [<b>Ulrich
von Hutten</b>] was then only thirty-five and when he died his pen was his only
possession.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Even the sword of this
brave <i>miles Christianus </i>was gone."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[128-129] [end of chapter VI].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>VIII<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">PIRCKHEIMER </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[Willibald
Pirckheimer 1470 â€“ 1530]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Speculative Patrician</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>["155"]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'Right on the market place, opposite
the "SchÃ¶ner Brunnen," in the heart of the city [<b>Nuremberg</b>]
stood his [<b>Pirckheimer</b>] <b>magnificent patrician house</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was, as <b>Celtis</b> put it, a hospice
for erudite men.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>At his table dined
many leading figures of the day </b>[compare:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Baron d' Holbach 1723 â€“ 1789, and his dinner parties, which "at
firstâ€¦were modeled on the parties he attended at Leyden."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>("Stanford Encyclopedia of
Philosophy" (online))]<b>â€”Luther, Melanchthon, Celtis, Hutten,
Regiomontanus, Galeazzo di San Severino, Leonardo da Vinci's sponsor in Milan,
and others.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The list of his
correspondents reads like a dictionary of <b>Renaissance scholars</b>, or like
the index of <b>Trithemius</b>' <i>De viris illustribus</i>, and includes such
names as <b>Erasmus, Spalatin, Beatus Rhenanus, David de Marchello, Giovanni
Francesco Pico della Mirandola, and Zwingli.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Pirckheimer stalked books like a hunter and <o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">518<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">had
</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">as his game room <b>one of the best
libraries of the time</b>, partly inherited, collected from churches and
monasteries, gifts and inheritances from friends, and purchases from the book
fairs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It included especially many
Aldine Greek editions,<sup>4</sup> so that <b>in 1504 Pirckheimer could with
some plausibility boast of owning all the Greek books printed in Italy.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Pirckheimer</b> was a literary arbiter,
indefatigable translator, and a patron par excellence.<sup>5</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[156].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>IX<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">ERASMUS </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[Desiderius
Erasmus c. 1466 â€“ 1536]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Philosopher of Christ<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus as the prince of the
Northern humanists was titular head also of German humanism.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He did not wish to be identified with any
national group, for, he wrote to <b>Zwingli</b>, "I desire to be a citizen
of the world, common to all, or rather, a stranger to all."<sup>1</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To a Brabant countryman he once repeated <b>Cicero</b>'s
words:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>Where you fare well,
there is your fatherland.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In
1520 he replied to <b>Peter Manius</b>, who had urged him to declare openly
that he was a German and not a Frenchman so that Germany might not be deprived
of this great glory, that it seemed to him to make little difference where a
man is born.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is a vain sort of
glorification, he felt, when a city or nation boasts of producing a man who has
become great through his own exertions and not by the help of his
fatherland.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For the country which has
made him great has a better right to boast than that which brought him forth.<sup>2<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></sup>....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>["197"].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>The story of Erasmus is so
common that, to turn a phrase from Chaucer, every wit that hath discretion
knows all or part of it.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>And yet <b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Erasmus remains elusive, a proteus, a man of a
hundred faces</span>.</b><sup>6</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Immortalized
by Holbein, Quentin Metsys, and DÃ¼rer</b>, he looks out from the canvas with an
enigmatic half-smile, an expression suggesting the complications of his
personality (figure 10).<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Small wonder
that straightforward <b>Frederick of Saxony</b> commented that this was an
amazing little man, for <b>one never knows where one stands with</b> [<b>Erasmus</b>]
him.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was gifted with a quick and
ready wit, with unusual charm and brilliance.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>For all his correspondence and superficial gregariousness, </b>he<b> </b>[<b>Erasmus</b>]
<b>was a lonely monarch who gave of himself without reservations to no one.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was no confessor, no fighter, no great
man.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He abhorred disturbances to the
point of appearing to many contemporaries to be a timorous neuter.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was a valetudinarian, loving good living
and creature comforts, petulant, querulous, flattering, deceptive, and
vindictive.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He saw his own weakness and
feared that in <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">519<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">case
of a conflict he would like Peter deny his friends.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He could speak almost disinterestedly of the tragic deaths of his
friends <b>Fisher</b> and <b>More</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"Not all have sufficient strength for martyrdom," he
confided.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>In a call for world
missions in 1535</b> he expressed the wish that God would have given to him the
spirit of martyrdom.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But such
dedication and courage were never granted to him.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus</b> <b>justified his lack
of a heroic spirit with the comment that there have been many martyrs in
Christendom but only a few scholars.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Erasmus</b> was primarily precisely that, a scholar.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was not a historian, a philosopher, a
scientist, a painter, or a musician.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He
was not a discoverer, one of those Renaissance men like <b>Columbus,
Copernicus,</b> or <b>Vesalius</b> who achieved a break-through to a new world,
but he was a scholar in temperament and calling, editing and writing with a
phenomenal ascetic capacity for long, hard work.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He frequently worked hurriedly, standing on one foot, as he once
put it.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the <i>Colloquies</i> he
referred to himself as one of those prolific writers who never ceased to make
war with the pen.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He [<b>Erasmus</b>] <b>successfully
evaded all practical responsibility in church and state in order to be free for
his books.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>He lived in his study
and died in his bed.</b><sup>7</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[198-199].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Erasmus' attitude toward the
papacy provides a clear-cut example of his consistency within ambivalence.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For <b>Erasmus</b> the papacy incorporated
the essence of the church, and yet he reserved some of his most savage thrusts
for the popes.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>As spiritual shepherd
the pope was above all mortals, possessing heavenly authority.<sup>23</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His attacks on the papacy were consistently
leveled against individual popes, usually in their secular, political, or
military capacity, their theatrical splendor and wastefulness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>At the same time he stressed obedience to
the pope as ecclesiastical head and as capstone of the hierarchy.<sup>24</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The church was for him itself the communion
of believers who agree in faith in the gospel, who honor the one Father, who
found their whole trust in his Son, and who are led by the Holy Spirit himself.<sup>25</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Since the church is embodied in the papacy,
whoever does not recognize the pope stands outside the church.<sup>26</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus</b> complained most bitterly
against the pope for stirring up war between the Christian princes instead of
acting as peacemaker.<sup>27</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But
worst of all were the popes who themselves made war and in this none compared
with <b>Julius II</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"The
highest pontiff <b>Julius</b> wages war," <b>Erasmus</b> once reported in
words reminiscent of <b>Hutten</b>, having seen his triumphal entry into <b>Bologna</b>,
"he conquers, triumphs, and acts entirely like <b>Julius</b> [<b>Caesar</b>]."<sup>28</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus</b> <b>held that terms like</b>
Apostle, shepherd, bishop, abbot, pope, were concepts of a holy office, not of
secular overlordship, the title for an office of Christian faith and love, <b>not
for earthly power and might.</b><sup>29</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[205].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">520<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>The Reformation was an intense personal tragedy
for Erasmus. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>At the height of his
fame when <b>Luther</b> appeared on the scene, <b>Erasmus</b> <b>suddenly found
himself caught in the middle like the man, he said, who in trying to separate
two gladiators met his death.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"<b>I am a heretic to both sides,</b>" he [<b>Erasmus</b>] <b>lamented.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He would sooner have remained a
spectator.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The combat and general
disturbance of the conflict pained him, although had he lived to see the
evangelicals build an orderly and well-regulated church life in the decades
after the decisive battles, he might have felt differently.<sup>117</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus had contributed much to the
Reformation, as both friend and foe knew very well. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>His criticisms of abuse, his stress on going
to the sources, his Biblical and patristic scholarship, and his spiritualism as
opposed to formalism were all positive contributions.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Even after <b>Erasmus</b> took his stand against <b>Luther</b>,
he refused to condemn him on all counts and continued to duel as fiercely with <b>such
Catholic foes as ZuÃ±iga, Aleander, Alberto Pio, Lee, Latomus,</b> and <b>Bedda</b>
as with the reformers.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b>,
in turn, <b>continued to buy and read Erasmus' books long after their formal
break.</b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[230-231].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>X<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">LUTHER </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[Martin
Luther 1483 â€“ 1546]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">The Reformer</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>["237"]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>Through
many of Luther's exclamations in which he calls for a renewal of learning rings
the tone of cultural nationalism</b> familiar from <b>Wimpfeling, Celtis,
Hutten, and Pirckheimer.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>Luther</b>] We have
unfortunately rotted and spoiled long enough in darkness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>We have been German brutes far too long. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Let
us for once use our reason</span></b> so that God notices our thankfulness for
his good gifts and <b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">so that other
countries see that we are also human beings and people who can either learn
something from them or can teach them, so that the world is improved also
through us!</span></b><sup>17</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Luther believed that human
culture of the highest literary and artistic quality existed by its own right
as part of the order of creation.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[243].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>"<b>Luther asserted that Cicero, the
darling of the humanists, was invincibly ignorant about God</b> [Cicero
wrote:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>On the Nature of the Gods </i>(<i>De
Natura Deorum</i>)]<b>.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To be sure
he [<b>Cicero</b>] knew everything that natural reason and <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">human
powers could assemble, but he was ignorant of what God wills and of his
feelings toward us men.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Reason is
ignorant of this unless enlightened by the Holy Spirit through the Word.<sup>22</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Human culture does not make men true man as <b>Christ</b>
was true man, without sin and spiritually alive to God.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>As a matter of value judgment <b>Luther</b>
gave priority to the work of the <i>Spiritus Sanctus</i> over human <i>ingenium</i>,
to stammering religious truth over shining human eloquence, to<b> Christian
faith over antique learning.</b><sup>23</sup>"<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>[244-245].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[Luther (and
this author (Lewis W. Spitz))â€”preaching Christianism
("Christianity")!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Much
