<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>Luther
shared with the humanists a high regard for and even a fascination with
languages.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Medieval man had held
language to be a special divine gift and the humanists had been enthusiastic
over the power of the classical languages to unlock arcane meanings of the
texts.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For <b>Luther</b> the utility of
languages was functional and not[?] substantive[?].<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He [<b>Luther</b>] <b>expressed his views on this subject in one
of his Table Talks </b>[tischreden]<b> in this way:</b><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>Luther</b>]<b>
</b>Are the instruments of the arts and of nature useful to the
theologian?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>One knife cuts better than
another.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Thus good tools, such as
languages and the arts, can teach more clearly.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Now many, like <b>Erasmus</b>, have the arts and languages, and,
nevertheless, err most perniciously...<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>But the thing must be distinguished from its abuse...<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is the same tongue before faith and after
faith, and language insofar as it is language does not help faith, but
nevertheless it serves it when the heart is enlightened.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Thus reason also serves faith in that it
reflects on a thing, how it has been illuminated.<sup>38</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[253].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>Luther</b>
<b>made use of the humanists' philological techniques, their textual
discoveries, and their linguistic and grammatical works.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>One finds in his New Testament commentaries
phrases like, </b>"<b>as Erasmus correctly translates.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is well known that he used <b>LefÃ¨vre d'
Ã‰taples</b>' glosses on the Psalms and Epistles, that he changed in the middle
of his lectures on Romans to <b>Erasmus' <i>Novum Testamentum</i></b> for a
Greek text, and that as a man of almost supreme linguistic ability he mastered
Greek and became a respectable student of Hebrew in order to facilitate his
translations and exegesis.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His
knowledge of Hebrew, made possible by the pioneer work of <b>Pellican, Reuchlin</b>,
and <b>Jewish scholars such as David Kimchi and Moses Kimhi</b>, enabled him to
work effectively with the <b>Old Testament</b> and also to recognize the <b>Hebraisms
in the New</b>.<sup>42</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Like the
humanists he heaped scorn on the Quadriga, as a typical passage from his [<b>Luther's</b>]
second commentary on Galatians (1535) illustrates:<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">[Luther]
<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">The idle and unlearned monks and the
school doctors</span> deemed...that the Scripture has four senses: </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span><b>the literal sense, the moral sense, the
allegorical sense, and the mystical sense</b> [["Quadriga" (usage?):]
Literalem, Tropologicum, Allegoricum, et Anagogicum]; and according to these
senses they have foolishly interpreted almost all the words of the
Scripturesâ€”as:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>this word
"Jerusalem" literally signified that city which was so named:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>morally a pure conscience:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>allegorically the church militant:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>mystically the celestial city or the Church
triumphant.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>With these trifling and
foolish fables they rent the Scriptures into so many and diverse senses, that
silly poor consciences could receive no doctrine at all.</b><sup>43</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Like <b>Erasmus</b> and the medieval
tradition <b>Luther</b> held that a doctrine or a controverted point cannot be
proved by allegory.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But it goes without
saying that those <b>Old Testament</b> passages given an allegorical
interpretation in the <b>New Testament</b> were to be understood in both the
literal and the allegorical sense....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[255].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[serious stuffing, for <b>Mental
Horror Vacui</b> (see christianism.com, 2896-2938)].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'Because
he [<b>Luther</b>] <b>was a full-time and professional exegete</b> with vastly
greater influence in this field than any of the German humanists and because he
pressed for the historical and literal interpretation as a basis for theological
exegesis, <b>Luther more than Wimpfeling, Reuchlin, or even Erasmus deserves
the title</b> "<b>father of modern exegesis.</b>"'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[257].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>through
his German Bible Luther</b> gave new impetus to the rising ascendancy of the
middle and north German vocabulary and accent which created the language of
modern German literature.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Friedrich
Nietzsche</b> in <i>Beyond Good and Evil</i> acknowledges that "<b>Luther's
Bible was the best German book up to then.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>It was an achievement of unparalleled importance in German
literary history.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[262].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Painting and sculpturing were
adversely affected by the Reformation</b>, since the incentive to erect sacred
statues and the employment of artists for scenes from the lives of the saints
disappeared.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The literary humanists
from <b>Erasmus</b> on down had showed a peculiar indifference to the grat
glories of Renaissance art.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther
fits into this general pattern</b>, but more because of his preoccupation with
theology than with classical or early Christian literary remains, as was true
in the case of he humanists.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b>
supported the move characteristic of painting from <b>Giotto</b> on away from
the Byzantine etherealization <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">of
the <b>Virgin Mary</b>, commenting that to portray the Virgin as completely
noble detracted from the reality of the contrast between the glory which Christ
left and the lowly unworthiness to which he came.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He was opposed to elaborateness and gaudiness for "in human
weakness and nothingness God's power is particularly revealed."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>he once remarked that he wished he could
paint on all the houses in <b>Wittenberg</b> "pictures from the Word of
God which would help men realize what God has done for us in Christ."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He believed that religious paintings are not
a kind of fetish or superstition, but rather symbols and a means of
proclamation, praise, and thanks through which the church communicates its
message to the viewer.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther
appreciated the work of the two Cranachs, of Hans Baldung Grien, and especially
of DÃ¼rer's better students, to do the illustrations for his translation of the

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>The
great body of German Protestant church music owes its being to Luther's love of
music and his remarkably high standards.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>[263].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'In
his early theological lectures <b>Luther</b>, too, drew heavily upon patristic
exegesis.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But later he wrote of the <b>church
fathers</b>:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"As many as there
were, all of them failed either to observe or thoroughly and correctly to
understand the kingdom of grace through Christ."<sup>62</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[256-266].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'In his great play <i>Agamemnon</i>,
<b>Aeschylus</b> wrote this classic line, "<b>Suffering is the road to
learning; learning comes only through suffering; if you want to learn you have
to suffer in order to do your learning.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b> experienced the bitter truth of those words in the
course of his soul struggle, but the religious lesson that he learned was to
let God be God, and that His mercy endures forever.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He learned a lesson regarding man which he once expressed with
epigrammatic force in a letter to <b>Spalatin</b>, June 30, 1530:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>We should be men and not God.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>That is the sum of it.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For those contemporary German humanists who
lacked what <b>Kierkegaard</b> was later to call "<b>a certain
strenuousness of mental and moral effort</b>," he had only disdain.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The nation, and particularly the men of the
younger generation, followed <b>Luther</b>, for he sounded a more certain
trumpet.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The words which <b>Bugenhagen</b>,
a man of no mean classical learning, <b>spoke over Luther's dead body</b>
reflected his conviction that there lay not just a professor, a scholar, or
humanist, but a prophet:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"He [<b>Martin
Luther</b>] was without doubt that angel of God of which the Apocalypse speaks
in chapter fourteenâ€”flying in midheaven with an eternal gospel to proclaim to
those who dwell on earth...<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">This
angel said 'Fear God and give him glory!'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Those
are the two parts of <b>Dr. Martin Luther</b>'s teaching, the law and the

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>XI<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">CONCLUSION<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>"<b>A man will,</b>" <b>Dr.
Johnson </b>[Samuel Johnson 1709 â€“ 1784]<b> remarked,</b> "<b>turn over
half a library to make one book.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The publications, personal correspondence, and private papers of the
humanists have provided some insight into their religious mentality and reform
programs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It remains now to step back
and to ask the right general questions about the meaning of all this.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The once heatedly debated issue of the <b>Renaissance</b>
as Christian[later pagan] or pagan, never really relevant to the Northern
scene, obviously has no meaning at all for German humanism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The [<b>These</b>] <b>humanists were all
Christians, in their way, pious, and all had Christian deaths and burials.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The two who died without benefit of clergy, <b>Pirckheimer</b>
and <b>Erasmus</b>, did not do so by choice but of necessity.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The most important questions for religious
history are much more difficult to pose.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>This is necessarily so, for these men lived in a time of tremendous
intellectual and spiritual as well as economic and social change.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Theirs was a land alive with movements of
religious protest and reform.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Theirs<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>was a day which first brought to light the
tensions between the classical and Christian components of their culture.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Theirs</b> [Christian humanists] <b>was a
generation brimming with vitality and creativity, yet tormented and tentative.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The German historian <b>Georg von
Below</b> [1858 â€“ 1927] remarked that he believed more had been written on the
causes of the <b>Reformation</b> than on the <b>Reformation</b> itself.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The question of the origins of the so-called
<b>Northern Renaissance</b> has also intrigued historians and has provoked an
extensive literature.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This study of the
leading German humanists sheds additional light upon the more limited problem
of <b>the origins of German humanism</b>....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>["267"].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">525<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>The Culture of the High Renaissance</i>,
Ancients and Moderns, In Sixteenth-Century Rome, Ingrid D. Rowland</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, Cambridge University Press, 1999 (1998).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b><i>Introduction</i><o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[Ãˆ] sempre suto non altrimenti periculoso trovare
modi ed ordini nuovi che si fusse cercare acque e terre incognite.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">It has always been just as dangerous to find new ways
and orders of doing things as to go in search of new lands and seas.<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Machiavelli
</b>[1469 â€“ 1527], Preface to<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:
2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><i>Discourses
on the First Decade of Titus Livius<o:p></o:p></i></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Paradoxically,
<b>Italy's jolt into the modern era began with a long, penetrating look into
the past.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The fifteenth- and
sixteenth-century thinkers who hailed a rebirth of ancient values in their own
time did so knowing that their own era was irrevocably distinct from antiquity;
indeed, <b>all but the most fanatical wanted their Renaissance to stay in the
heady realms of fiction.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For the
world that generated the antiquarian movement known as "humanism" was
a world of rapidly developing commerce, commerce that depended absolutely on
modern inventions, modern navigation, and modern mathematics.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>At the same time, the shapers of that modern
world also felt the need to have it incorporate the best elements of their
forebears' existence.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>With a
rationality born perhaps of commercial training, they probed the past for its
systems, what they called "modi e ordini" (ways and orders) or
"ragione" (method), hoping to recover the abstract principles that
would give their own achievements enduring value.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Nowhere was this paradoxical search for higher principles more
intense than in papal Rome.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
suggestive atmosphere of the city, with its endless layers of civilization,
inspired the officials of the late fifteenth- and early sixteenth-century
papacy, self-consciously charged with carrying out God's mission on earth, to
believe that in their lifetimes for once humanity could muster the political
means, the historical wisdom, and the living talent necessary to create
"new ways and orders" of lasting validity, enfolding the best of all
that had gone before in a truly catholic embrace.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>This is the story of that concerted
attempt to derive a new order for the future from scrutiny of the past.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The search
for systems was not itself systematic, nor did the seekers share the same idea
of their goal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was a fiction, after
all, often a personal fiction.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Nonetheless, a common theme unites <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">many
of the disparate activities that went into the creation of <b>Renaissance <o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">526<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Rome</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>And the
paradoxical quest for a new order, by its very oxymoronic challenge, invited
ingenious responses.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>On occasionâ€”most notably, perhaps,
in the visual artsâ€”this utopian project actually succeeded, producing such
expressive innovations as the conscious gradations of style (<i>modi</i>) that
appear in the painting of <b>Raphael </b>and <b>Michelangelo</b>, and the
"orders" of classical architecture, devised in antiquity but first
described as orders in sixteenth-century <b>Rome</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Yet the same search for new ways and orders also made itself felt
in the world of finance, as when banker <b>Agostino Chigi</b> tried, like a nineteenth-century
industrialist, to establish an international economic monopoly on a single
commodity.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Chigi</b>'s vision took
form because at the same time his pope, <b>Julius II</b>, was working toward
another international goal:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>asserting a
universal church that would far exceed the ancient Roman empire in scope.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Indeed, <b>Julius II</b> was the pope who
felt the synthetic drive of his epoch more powerfully than any other; the
papacy of his successor <b>Leo X</b> provided some reflective respite from the
momentum of <b>Julius</b>'s headlong pontificate, but it also began to reveal
the fragility inherent in any synthesis of old and new.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[1-2].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'It was the friends of the
Neapolitan <b>Cardinal Oliviero Carafa</b>, who foregathered in his house on <b>Piazza
Navona</b>, who first began to dress a battered old Roman statue group of
heroes from Homer's <i>Iliad</i>â€”a noseless <b>Menelaus </b>holding the
headless, limbless trunk of the dead <b>Patroclus</b>â€”in fanciful costume on <b>Saint
Mark's Day</b>, praising this singular apparition in verse as "<b>Mastro
Pasquino</b>" and giving rise to a still unbroken tradition of social
commentary, the <b>pasquinade</b> (Fig. 5 [see below]), a poetic form in which
the statue himself speaks his mind in verse on events of the day.<sup>55</sup>
[see "Notes", 530]<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In 1501, <b>Cardinal
Carafa </b>enshrined the talking statue on a pedestal, the better to display
his costumes and the cranky poems affixed to his raddled [for simplicity:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>worn] surface at every opportunity.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The cardinal's house is gone, but <b>Pasquino</b>
continues to pique Roman consciences; he <b>spent much of the 1980s with a
spray-painted feminist graffito on his pedestal that read</b> "<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Pasquina</span>.</b>"'</span>&nbsp; <span style="font-family:Arial">[28-29].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<i>Figure
5</i>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Pasquino.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Engraving by Antoine LafrÃ©ry </b>[<b>1550</b>]<b>.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Courtesy of the University of Chicago
Libraries."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[after page 146].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>THE SISTINE CHAPEL CEILING</b> (<b>1508â€“1512</b>)<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Michelangelo</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> finally succumbed to the pope's [<b>Julius II</b>]
persuasion in 1508.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was to finish,
with a bad crick in his neck and a frazzled temper, in 1512.<sup>64</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">527<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Like<b>
Pinturicchio</b>'s frescoes for the Borgia Apartments, and like the earlier
fresco cycle commissioned by <b>Sixtus IV</b> for the <b>Sistine Chapel</b>
walls, the <b>Sistine Chapel</b> ceiling used visual images to set the Church
within the scheme of universal history, but the difference in scale between <b>Michelangelo</b>'s
work and that of his forerunners was epochal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The <b>Sistine Chapel</b> walls, which had surely been conceived in the
1480s according to a plan devised by <b>Pope Sixtus</b> himself, <b>traced
parallel lives of Moses and Christ</b>, showing how every aspect of the life of
<b>Moses</b> among the <b>Egyptians</b> and <b>Hebrews</b> prefigured some
aspect of the life of <b>Christ</b> and the Church.<sup>65</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The finding of <b>Moses</b> in the bulrushes
prefigured the Nativity; <b>Christ</b>'s baptism was prefigured by the
circumcision of <b>Moses</b>' son; and, most emphatically for the whole scheme,
<b>Moses' handing down the Law foreshadowed Christ's handing over the keys of
authority to Saint Peter.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[160].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>PARODY:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>ERASMUS AND ARETINO<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">An
earlier barbarian visitor to Rome had been equally disconcerted by the dream
world in which the Curia seemed to pass much of its time.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus of Rotterdam passed through Rome
in 1507</b>, where he made some good friends, including <b>Fedro Inghirami</b>,
and received some very bad impressions.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>He complained about a sermon that sounded more like an oration at a
pagan sacrifice than part of a Christian liturgy, and he was appalled at <b>Julius</b>'s
militancy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>When the pope died, <b>Erasmus</b>
wrote a bitterly funny dialogue called <b><i>Julius exclusus de caelo</i></b></span>
(<b><span style="font-family:Arial">Julius shut out of heaven </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[see 377-383, 528-529]), in which the pope storms the
Pearly Gates in clanking armor and wonders why <b>Saint Peter</b> <b>refuses to
let him in:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Julius:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>My bile's boiling.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I'll knock on the gates.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Hey!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Hey!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Someone open up this
portal.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What's going on?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>No one's shown up?<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Peter:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>It's a good thing we have a gate of
adamant ["extremely hard substance"], otherwise, he would have broken
it, whatever he is...maybe a giant?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>a
satrap?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>a sacker of cities!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But, O, immortal gods, what sewer do I smell
here?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I won't open the gates just yet,
but I'll look out of this barred window and see what kind of a monster it
is.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Who are you?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What do you want?<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>...Tell me who you are.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>J:</b><i><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></i>As if
you couldn't tell.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>P:</b><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Tell?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I see a sight never before seen, not to say
a monster! <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">528<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">J:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Quit this nattering, if you know
what's good for you...In case you didn't know, I'm Julius the Ligurian, and
unless I'm mistaken, you're familiar with the two letters P.M.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>P:</b><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>I'll bet
they mean Pestiferus Maximus.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>J:</b><span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>No!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Pontifex Maximus!<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">P:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>You're like a great king,
greater than Thrice Great Hermes, but you're not getting in here; the place is
holy.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">J:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>So you won't open up?<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">P:</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>I'd rather open to anyone
but such a pest as you.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But do you want
some good advice?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>You have a handful of
strong men and a heap of money.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>You're
a good builder.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Make yourself a new
paradise, but fortify it well so the devils don't take it.<sup>7</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.5in;text-indent:-1.0in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus's response to the
Parnassian reveries of the circle around Leo X and Pietro Bembo was still more
savagely comic; his dialogue called </b>"<b>The Ciceronian</b>" (<i>Ciceronianus</i>)
<b>was published in 1525</b>, a vicious parody of <b>the</b> <b>epistolary
exchange between Gianfrancesco Pico and Pietro Bembo</b> on imitation.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The letters had been made widely available
in print with <b>Johann Frobenius</b>'s Basel edition of 1518 and may have been
available in manuscript still earlier; <b>Erasmus </b>certainly composed his
dialogue after having read them carefully.<sup>8</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He also drew, with still more evident
feeling, on his own memories of life in Rome:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"I will report...what I heard with these ears; what I saw with
these eyes."<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Predictably, however, <b>the most
savage of all the parodists of Leonine Rome was no remote observer like Erasmus</b>
but a character who could usually be found plunged into the thick of the city's
activity, a man who served for three years as <b>Agostino Chigi's Tuscan
houseboy, Pietro Aretino</b> (1492â€“1556).<sup>9</sup><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He came into <b>Chigi</b>'s service in 1517, already gifted with
a sharp tongue and a ready pen, gifts that found ample encouragement in the
magnate's Viridario [Italian.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Latin:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>viridarium:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"pleasure-garden or green court of an
ancient Roman villa or palace" (<i>O</i>.<i>E</i>.<i>D</i>.)]; so did <b>Aretino</b>'s
propensity for outrageous sexual humor.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Despite his genuine affection for <b>Chigi</b>, <b>Aretino</b> came into
Rome as part of a diffident new generation, one too young to have been affected
either by <b>Julius II</b>'s apostolic zeal or by the more muted energy
generated during the first years of <b>Leo X</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Aretino</b> <b>had a rare nose for decadence, and the later
years of Leonine </b>[Leo X]<b> Rome offered it in abundance.</b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[247-248].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">529<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:81.0pt;text-indent:-81.0pt;tab-stops:
.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"["<b>Notes</b>"] 55<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>For the statue of Pasquino</b>, see <b>Cesare
D'Onofrio</b>, <i>Un Popolo di statue racconta storie fatti leggende della
cittÃ  di Roma antica medievale moderna </i>(Rome:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Romana SocietÃ  Editrice, 1990), 27â€“43.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>A lively collection of sixteenth-century pasquinades is to be
found in <b>Antonio Marzo, ed., <i>Pasquino e dintorni</i></b> (Rome:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Salerno, 1990).<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>See also <b>V. Marucci, A. Marso, and A. Romano, <i>Pasquinate
romane del Cinquecento</i></b> (Rome:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Salerno, 1983)<b>;</b> <b>Giovanni Antonio Cesareo, <i>Pasquino e
pasquinate della Roma di Leone X</i> </b>[see 258], Miscellanea della Reale
Deputazione Romana di Storia Patria, no. 11 (Rome:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Reale Deputazione Romana di Storia Patria, <b>1938</b>)."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[262].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">530<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Erasmus and the Humanists</i>, Albert
Hyma</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, University of Michigan, F.S.
Crofts, 1930.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Historical
Introduction</span></b>" [1]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">Erasmus spoke in the year 1515 as hundreds of well-known churchmen
have spoken in the twentieth century.</span></b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>In his opinion it mattered little whether the miracles recorded
in the Bible had actually happened or not.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>As for the doctrines of transubstantiation, of purgatory, and of
justification by faith and works, he believed that they might be interpreted in
various ways.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He thought it was very
foolish for anybody to stake his career on the definition of doctrines, and he
said on many occasions that <b>to imitate the life of Jesus was far more
important than to argue about dogma.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Those who considered him a coward lost sight of his great intellectual
capacity.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">As
Henry Charles Lea </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[1825 â€“ 1909]<b>
has aptly said,</b> <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Erasmus, when rightly considered, was one of
the most heroic figures of an age of heroes.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Nowhere else can we find an instance so marked of the power of pure
intellect.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His gift of ridicule was the
most dreaded weapon in Europe and he used it mercilessly upon the most profitable
abuses of the Church.</span></b>"'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[1]
[end of "Historical Introduction"].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:

mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>The Protestant Reformation</i>,
1517â€“1559, Lewis W. Spitz </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[1922 â€“
1999], Stanford University, Illustrated, Harper &amp; Row, <b>c1985</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>During the 1520s a group of
Cambridge dons met to discuss the new Protestant ideas at the White House Inn,
which came to be known as</b> "<b>Little Germany.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This coterie provided the key leaders of the
movement in England: <span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Robert Barnes</span>, John Frith, Hugh
Latimer, Thomas Bilney, Nicholas Ridley, <span style="text-transform:uppercase">John
Bale</span>, John Foxe, and possibly William Tyndale. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>Some of them were martyred or exiled by <b>Henry
VIII</b> and some fell victim to "<b>bloody Mary</b>."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Thomas Becon</b> [c. 1511 â€“ 1567] paid
them tribute in the preface to <i>The Flower of Godly Prayers:</i><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>Becon</b>]
God, once again having pity on this realm of England, raised up His prophets,
namely <b>William Tyndale, Thomas Bilney, John Frith, Doctor</b> [<b>Robert</b>]
<b>Barnes, Jerome </b>[<b>Barlowe</b>]<b>,</b> [<b>Thomas</b>] <b>Garret, with
divers others</b>, which both with their writings and sermons earnestly labored
to call us unto repentance that by this means the fierce wrath of God might be
turned away from us.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But how were they
entreated?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>How were their painful
labors regarded?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>They themselves
were condemned and burnt as heretics, and their books condemned and burnt as
heretical.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></b>O most unworthy act!<sup>11</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The person-to-person spread of
the evangelical movement was chronicled by John Foxe in his <i>Book of Martyrs</i>.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He reported that it was through <b>Tyndale</b>
that <b>Frith</b> "received into his heart the seed of the Gospel and
sincere godliness."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In 1524 <b>Latimer</b>
presented a bachelor of divinity thesis directed against <b>Melanchthon</b>,
but <b>Bilney</b> persuaded him of the rightness of the Lutheran position.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In order to build the faculty of his new
college at Oxford, in 1526 <b>Cardinal Wolsey</b> brought scholars from
Cambridge, but six of the eight appointees were from the reform-minded group.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Tyndale was the most effective
propagandist for Protestantism in England.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Thomas More considered him his most dangerous opponent.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Born about 1495 in Gloucestershire, he took
an M.A. at Oxford and continued his study at Cambridge.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He felt the need for a good translation of
the Bible and after attempting without success to persuade <b>Bishop Turnstall</b>
to permit him to render the New Testament into English, he traveled in 1524 to
Wittenberg.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Influenced by Luther's
German version, he published in Worms the first printed English translation of
the New Testament.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>During the next
years he collaborated with <b>Miles Coverdale</b> in translating large parts of
the <b>Old Testament</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The Bible and
his tracts were smuggled into England.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In his later years <b>Tyndale</b> lived in the English house of the
Merchant Adventurers of <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">532<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Antwerp,
where he was immune from arrest by the Habsburg imperial officials.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Thomas More</b> <b>plotted for his
death.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In May, 1535, Tyndale was
tricked into leaving the house by an Englishman who posed as a convert. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>He was arrested and imprisoned in a castle
near Brussels.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Sixteen months later he
[<b>Tyndale</b>] <b>was tried for heresy and on October 6, 1536</b> [Erasmus
died July 12, 1536]<b>, he was strangled at the stake and his body burned to
ashes.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>His last words are said to
have been:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Lord, open the king of
England's eyes."<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The fiery-tempered prior Robert
Barnes</b> [close friend of John Bale] provided another personal link with <b>Wittenberg</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>On Christmas Eve, 1525, he delivered an
impassioned sermon in which he leveled twenty-five criticisms at the church and
made heretical statements.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Wolsey</b>
had his Cambridge rooms searched for Lutheran books which <b>Barnes</b>
foresightedly had hidden elsewhere.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>On
the advice of <b>Bishops Gardiner and Foxe</b> he abjured his preaching
"against the wordliness of the church" and did penance by kneeling
during <b>Bishop John Fisher</b>'s sermon at St. Paul's Cathedral on February
11, 1526.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In addition, he was forced to
carry a faggot in procession around the church.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Under house arrest in 1528, he dressed in lay clothes and fled
via Antwerp to Wittenberg.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>There he
became a guest and close friend of Luther.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>In 1531 the <b>Wittenberg</b> theologians sent him as their
representative to <b>Henry VIII</b>, but <b>Chancellor Thomas More </b>attempted
to have him arrested as a heretic and apostate monk.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He escaped by disguising himself as a merchant.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>During the last conservative years of <b>Henry</b>'s
reign, his luck ran out and, condemned to death for opposing <b>Bishop Gardiner</b>
and the king, he [<b>Robert Barnes</b>] <b>was burned at Smithfield on July 30,
1540.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In his final confession he
declared:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"I trust in no good
works that ever I did, but only in the death of Christ.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I do not doubt but through him to inherit
the kingdom of heaven."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Thus
did</b> "<b>St. Robert</b>" <b>die, as Luther affectionately called
him.</b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[246-248].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:

Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;

Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Luther and German Humanism</i>, Lewis W.
Spitz</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, Variorum, <b>1996</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>
