<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>I<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">THE RENAISSANCE:<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">HUMANISM AND HUMANISM RESEARCH<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial">I.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Definitions and Varieties<o:p></o:p></span></i></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></i><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Humanism, the most characteristic form of Renaissance
intellectual life, developed in Italy about the middle of the fourteenth
century and persisted through the Reformation period well into the seventeenth
century.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The term "<b>humanism</b>" or <b><i>umanesimo</i></b> was
coined by a German pedagogue, <b>F.J. Niethammer</b>, who used it in 1808 to
refer to a philosophy of education that favored classical studies in the school
curriculum.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Karl Hagen</b> in a work
published 1841â€“43 and <b>George Voigt</b>, 1859, first used the word <b><i>Humanismus</i></b>
as a historical event and an intellectual phenomenon in association with the <b>Renaissance</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The term itself is protean</b> and has
been used in varying modalities to describe a number of movements involving an
anthropocentric emphasis.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In a very
general way it was tied up with the rationalistic and humanitarian attitudes
cultivated by the <b>Enlightenment</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Early in the nineteenth century it was used for the so-called second
humanism of <b>Wilhelm von Humboldt</b> and his contemporaries, who made reason
and experience the sole touchstones of truth.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>It<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>has been identified with the
libertarian ideas of <b>John Stuart Mill</b> and at the other extreme has been
appropriated by Marxian socialists as the communist "progressive
humanism."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The twentieth century
has witnessed the development of the "new" or "third
humanism," represented by thinkers such as <b>Bertrand Russell</b> and <b>Corliss
Lamont</b>, militantly anthropocentric and not infrequently
anti-religious.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The term has been
associated with the attempt to develop a non-theistic religio-ethical
movement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Jean-Paul Sartre</b> and
others have argued for existential philosophy as a humanism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The term has been applied indiscriminately
to any and every appreciation of human values and is not infrequently confused
with simple humanitarianism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Historically,
however, humanism has been most often closely associated with the thought and
literary culture of the Renaissance.</b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>["1"-2].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">534<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>II<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">THE COURSE OF GERMAN HUMANISM</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>"<b>Luther considered the
Renaissance revival of learning a happy development preceding the coming of the
Reformation</b> just as John the Baptist once heralded the coming of
Christ.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Humanism made the
Reformation possible</b>, for the knowledge of the languages, the critical
handling of sources, the attack on abuses, the national feeling, the war on
scholasticism, and an army of young humanists who rallied to the evangelical
cause were indispensable preconditions for the success of the Reformation.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The Reformation in turn contributed to
the continuity, the broadening of influence, the increase in classical
learning, and the perpetuation of many humanist values into later centuries.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[51].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>Luther's
confrontation with Erasmus</b> over the theological issue of freedom of the
human will to keep the law perfectly and to accept <b>Christ as Savior</b> of
its own power did not prevent him from recommending to students <b>Erasmus</b>'s
humanist writings and did not lead him to discourage <b>Melanchthon</b>'s
continued correspondence with the prince of humanists.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b> could distinguish much more
clearly than most <b>Reformation</b> scholars in our day between a right
relationship with <b>God</b> of everlasting importance and the supreme benefits
of culture for the very limited time allotted to man in the here and
now."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[54].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>If
printing served humanism and reform, the humanists and reformers served
publishing in turn. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>There was a
steadily ascending curve in the volume of publications, but controversies
triggered great upsurges in the number of books and pamphlets published.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Like the <b>Savonarola</b> incident in
Florence, the <b>Reuchlin</b> affair in Germany, the <b>Carlstadt</b> skirmish
with the Thomists, the events of the Reformation opened the floodgates.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The number of books published in Germany
increased by ten times between the posting of the <b>Ninety-Five Theses </b>[the
tradition, <b>1517</b>] and the year <b>1524</b>, which marked the high tide in
the printing of religious and social treaties.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>On February 14, 1519, the humanist publisher Johannes Froben in Basel
wrote to Luther:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>Froben</b>]
We sent six hundred copies of your collected works which I published to France
and Spain.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>They are sold in Paris, read
and appreciated at the <b>Sorbonne</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>The book dealer Clavus of Pavia</b> took a sizable number to Italy to
sell them everywhere in the cities.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I
have sent copies also to England and Brabant and have only ten copies left in
the <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">535<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">storeroom.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I
have never had such good luck with a book.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>The more accomplished a man is, the more he thinks of you.</b><sup>115</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The statistics tell an exciting
tale of the proliferation and power of the press. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>Estimates vary, but a reasonable conjecture
is that 40,000 titles were published in Europe during the fifteenth
century.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If the average edition
numbered 250 volumes, and it may well have been closer to 300, <b>there must
have been a total of ten to twelve million incunabala</b> [books printed before
1501] <b>published</b>, many traditional medieval titles, but many also
humanist and classical texts.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>By the
year <b>1517</b> another ten million volumes were published, but by <b>1550</b>
under the pressure of the <b>Reformation</b> 150,000 more titles had been
published for a total of sixty million volumes.<sup>116</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Some 25,000 works were printed in Germany
before <b>1500</b>, not including broadsides and leaflets, but once the <b>Reformation</b>
was underway the annual number rose to five hundred and then to a
thousand.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In <b>Wittenberg</b> alone
over six hundred different works were published between the years <b>1518</b>
and <b>1523</b>, whereas in the British Isles the total for these years was
less than three hundred.<sup>117</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Classical learning and religious thought no longer contributed
exclusively to what <b>Vico</b> was to call "the conceit of the
learned," but became the property of an ever broader range of the literate
population.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The French humanist
Louis Le Roy rightly declared later in the sixteenth century:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>Louis
Le Roy</b>] Besides the restoration of learning, now almost complete, the
invention of many fine new things...has been reserved to this age.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Among these, printing deserves to be put
first....The invention has greatly aided the advancement of all
disciplines.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For it seems miraculously
to have been discovered in order to bring back to life more easily literature
which seemed dead.<sup>118</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther,
like Erasmus, was quick to see the power of the press</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, but he held that the message was still more
powerful than the medium.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>In 1522</b>
he [<b>Luther</b>] <b>wrote:</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"I have only put God's Word in motion through preaching and
writing.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The Word has done everything
and carried everything before it."'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[70-72].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>"<b>Just as the vitality of the
Italian Renaissance and the creativity of Italian humanism especially in
Florence and Venice is said to have lasted far beyond the <i>sacco di Roma</i></b>
(1527)<b>, so German humanism, too, remained a powerful cultural force in
alliance with the Reformation.</b><sup>122</sup><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Partially subsumed under the religious drive of the Reformation,
it received through the approbations of and amalgamation with the Reformation a
broader, deeper, and long lasting impact through the sixteenth and seventeenth
centuries.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The study of the course of
German humanism from the early fifteenth century to the <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">536<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">seventeenth
century demonstrates the tremendous continuity of that intellectual <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">movement.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The commonplace notion of a sharp break
between Renaissance and Reformation so far as humanism in intellectual and
cultural terms is concerned has proved to be a <i>fable convenue</i> which must
be relegated to the historians' shelves of outmoded curiosities along with the
idea of the Middle Ages as the dark ages or the Enlightenment as an
antihistorical period.</b><sup>123</sup>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[74].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"....<b>the
human spirit must not fare too well in this world, for creative genius responds
to suffering and conflict and grows dull with overmuch prosperity. </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>The <b>German humanists</b> such as <b>Reuchlin</b>
were fond of quoting the line from <b>Horace</b>, <i>Exegi monumentum aere
perennis</i>.<sup>125</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Compared
with the golden age of the <b>Italian Renaissance</b> it was indeed a monument
of bronze.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But it also had a lasting
quality, though it gave way in the end to the iron age of an industrial
society."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[76].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>VII<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">HEADWATERS OF THE REFORMATION<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial">Studia Humanitatis, Luther Senior, et Initia
Reformationis</span></i><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'....Relating
the intellectual forces contributing to the <b>Reformation</b> and those
operative in <b>Luther</b> sheds light upon the beginnings of both.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To acknowledge that <b>Luther</b>'s <i>Werdegang</i>
[development, growth, career, etc.] occurred in a specific intellectual context
by no means minimizes his emergence as a creative thinker and original mind, a
man who reshaped his inheritance and then reformed the church.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Dr. Oberman</b> allows for the
"X" in the equation, as <b>E. Gordon Rupp </b>put it in his beautiful
opening address to the <b>Third International Congress for Luther Research</b>,
"the point at which great men cease to be explained by heredity and
environment, and the thought world of their contemporaries."<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Dr. Oberman</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">
<b>is a man who, like Dr. Johnson, was born to grapple with libraries</b>, and
the notes reveal that he has done so.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I
find his methodology and conception of history most congenial to my own
personal predilection....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">["89"-90].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">537<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[<b>footnote</b> (not referenced above)] "<sup>2</sup>For
a list of the classical authors and Italian humanists whose works were
published in Germany between 1465 and <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">1500
and the classical and humanist authors printed in German translations up to <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">the
year 1520, <b>see Rudolph Hirsch, </b>"<b>Printing and the Spread of
Humanism in Germany:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The Example of
Albrecht von Eyb,</b>" <b><i>Renaissance Men and Ideas</i>, Robert
Schwoebel, ed.</b> (New York, 1971)<b>, pp. 28, 31.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Most of the classical and humanist authors
whom <b>Luther</b> cited frequently had been published in Germany by
1520."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[103].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[<b>part
of a footnote</b> (not referenced above)] "<b>For the most part Luther
considered Italians to be very superstitious and blind in their saint cults</b>"<b>.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[110].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">Erasmus remained for</span></b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">
him [<b>Luther</b>] <b>a nutcracker, or mockingbird, who did not take Christ
seriously</b></span><b>.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> considered <b>Erasmus</b>' <i>Copia</i> and <i>Adages
</i>to be of value but thought all else would perish.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther</b> was ready to relieve <b>Erasmus</b> of all
embarrassment <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">at
being considered a Lutheran, for it is clear that "<b>Erasmus believes
implicitly whatever Pope Clement VII believes.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus</b> remained for him the great
Epicurean.<sup>1</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>With the
single exception of Erasmus</b>, however, one finds many more references in <b>Luther</b>'s
later writings to <b>John Hus, Karlstadt, MÃ¼ntzer, and comets</b> than to all
the Renaissance humanists together.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[111-112].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>footnote</b> (not referenced
above)] '<sup>3</sup><i>W A Tr</i>, II, 8, no. 1248.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Richard M. Douglas, <i>Jacopo Sadoleto</i>, <i>1477â€“1547</i> <i>Humanist
and Reformer</i></b> [see 121] (Cambridge, Mass., 1959), p. 47.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The Commentary on Psalm 50 was <b>Sadoleto</b>'s
first exegetical work.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus
praised it but Luther found it to be untheological throughout</b>, insensitive
to the motive of grace, and neglectful of the role of Christ in the redemption
of man.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>P. 188:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Commenting on Sadoleto's letter to
Melanchthon Luther described the author as one </b>"<b>who was a papal
secretary for fifteen years, certainly an able and cultivated man... but
cunning and artful withal, in the Italian manner.</b>" See also Douglas,
pp. 25, 27, 253 n. 64, 114, 116â€“17, 134, 149.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>VIII<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">LUTHER AND HUMANISM</span></b><span style="font-family:
Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>"In terms of substance, what
was the contribution of humanism to <b>Luther</b>'s role as a theological and
religious reformer?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Bernd Moeller</b>
[born 1931] once stated with epigrammatic force:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>Without humanism no Reformation.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This assertion on the surface seems
problematical, for Renaissance humanism did not lead to a radical Reformation
in the Italy of <b>Petrarch, Bruni,</b> or <b>Ficino</b>, nor in the Spain of <b>Cardinal
Ximenes</b>, nor in the France of <b>BudÃ©, Bodin,</b> or <b>LefÃ¨vre d'Ã‰taples</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But <b>in the German context humanism was
clearly an essential precondition and a necessary catalyst for radical change.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The <b>Italian humanists </b>considered
scholastic theology, and some of them even Aristotelian natural science, to be
a foreign import coming from the ultramontanes.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The <b>German humanists</b> were increasingly repelled by
scholasticism, admired Italian humanism, but were patriotically <b>hostile to
the Italian church and its exploitation of the German people.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[83-84].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>X<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther's
Importance for<o:p></o:p></span></i></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial">Anthropological
Realism</span></i></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'There is a discernible difference
in the way in which the <b>English and French Enlightenment intellectuals and
the German <i>AufklÃ¤rung </i></b>[German:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"Enlightenment"]<b><i> </i>thinkers </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>related to <b>Luther's Reformation</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hume and Gibbon were contemptuous of the
theological concern of the reformers.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>It is a curious development to find that in England many of the
Victorians in the next century were critical of "<b>Luther</b>'s
rationalism and <b>Erastianism</b> [<b>from</b> <b>Thomas Erastus</b> 1524 â€“
1583] ["the state is supreme over the church" (Internet);
etc.]."<sup>7</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Voltaire
despised the Reformation as a </b>"<b>quarrel of monks</b>" and
sneered that "one cannot read without a mixture of contempt and pity the
manner in which <b>Luther</b> treats all his opponents and particularly the
Pope."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The men of the <i>AufklÃ¤rung</i>
were critical of Luther</b>, but by no means contemptuous.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>They were critical of the medieval remains
in his thought, but they were appreciative of his battle for the freedom of
conscience, which for them was the essence of the <b>Reformation</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In <b>Luther</b> the gold of religious and
ethical autonomy was still mixed with slag.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>They considered further purification and the completion of what<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">539<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> had begun to be their task.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was no mere theatrical gesture,
therefore, or act of cultural reform and resurgence.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>They staged "reformations" of dogmatics, jurisprudence,
orthography, the book trade, hymnbooks, and of Lutheranism hypocrisy, when the
men of the <b><i>AufklÃ¤rung</i></b> constantly called upon the name of <b>Luther</b>,
for they considered him to be the leader of the first attack wave, while they
constituted the phalanx of hoplites which would win the final victory of reason
over superstition and the forces of darkness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"<b>Reformation</b>" <b>became one of their favorite words</b>,
"reformation" as freedom and "reformation" as itself.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>the majestic <b>Goethe</b> [Johann Wolfgang
von Goethe 1749 â€“ 1832] in the <i>Frankfurter gelehrten Anzeigen</i> in 1772
mocked the "iconoclastic Zeal" of the "enlightened
reformers" of his day.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Hamann</b>
commented ironically on the "epidemic reformation swindle" and the
fact that "<b>reformation</b>" <b>was such a favorite word in the <i>AufklÃ¤rung</i></b>
[Enlightenment].<sup>8</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[139-140].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Feuerbach</b> [Ludwig Andreas
Feuerbach 1804 â€“ 1872] and <b>Schopenhauer</b> [Arthur Schopenhauer 1788 â€“
1860] in certain passages seem to be exploiting the authority of <b>Luther</b>
to support unorthodox positions in a conscious way.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This is a case of the tyranny, as <b>Lord Chesterfield</b> once
put it, which the living exercise over the dead.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>It is like <b>Kaiser Wilhelm</b> quoting <b>John Knox</b> to the
effect that "one man with God is always a majority."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther contributed to, but was also used
by, idealists and realists alike.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Both groups failed to appreciate his deepest
concerns, the primal anxiety and dread</span></b> (<i>Urgrauen</i>) <b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">which oppresses mortal man</span></b> [see
christianism.com, 2896-2938 (Horror Vacui)], the concern to find gracious the
God who is the final ground of being, the conviction that the divine initiative
changes man's being, makes of him a new creature, the theology of hope and
joy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Other moderns, the existentialists
and postliberal theologians have been able to wrestle more seriously with <b>Luther</b>'s
thought in its third and fourth dimensions [value?].'<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>[169].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>XI<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">MAN ON THIS ISTHMUS</span></b><span style="font-family:
Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>There were warnings in great
number, of course, from all of the</b> fathers [<b>Church Fathers</b>] <b>against
the lasciviousness of some classical writings and against the demonic nature of
the antique gods.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Tertullian</b>,
that dour rigorist, referred to the philosophers as the "patriarchs of
heresy" and blamed Greek philosophy for the Gnostic deviation.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He [<b>Tertullian</b>] <b>called</b> <b>Plato</b>
<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">a</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> "<b>grocery store for all the heretics</b>,"
and in the <i>De praescriptione</i><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">540<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial">haereticorum</span></i><span style="font-family:Arial"> he attacked <b>Plato</b>'s greatest student:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>Unhappy Aristotle who introduced
dialectic for the benefit of heresy</b>, the great master in building up and in
tearing down, ambiguous in its sentences, forced in its conjectures, ruthless
in its arguments; a work of contentions, a burden even for itself, it
discourses on everything so as not to have discoursed on anything."<sup>13</sup>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[28].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>The most celebrated document of despondency
over the human condition and the one against which</b> <b>Manetti</b>
[Giannozzo Manetti 1396 â€“ 1459 <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">(see <i>Two
Views of Man</i>, Pope Innocent III [when Cardinal Lotario dei Segni, 1195], <i><u>on
the Misery of Man</u></i>; Giannozzo Manetti, <i>on the Dignity of Man</i>,
translated, with an introduction, by Bernard Murchland, Ungar, c1966)] <b>was
reacting specifically was Innocent III's</b> [then, 1195, Cardinal [1190]
Lotario dei Segni (c. 1161 â€“ 1216) (Pope Innocent III, 1198 â€“ 1216)] <b><i><u>De
contemptu mundi seu de miseria humanae conditionis</u></i></b> [see 550]<b>, in
which he made the utmost of the dust-to-dust and ashes-to-ashes realities and
rehearsed the most disgusting side of human life:</b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>the lice, spittle, urine, feces, the brevity of time, old age,
the various labors and sorrows of mortals, the precariousness of life, the
constant nearness of death, the many kinds of torments and sufferings of the
human body, and his proclivities for sin and propensities for evil.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is true that <b>Innocent</b> planned to
write the corresponding essay on <b>the dignity of man</b>, but he was caught
up in administration and never rounded out the picture [Innocent III, after
those experiences, forgot about "the dignity of man"].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Thus the total effect of this writing from
such a lofty source was to underline in black the sorry side of human life.<sup>47</sup>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[42].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'....The
worry about man himself was well phrased by New England's poet laureate <b>Robert
Frost</b> [1874 â€“ 1963] when he said:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">You cannot frighten me
with your enormous spaces, It is the void </span></b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">[</span>see:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><a href="http://www.christianism.com/">www.christianism.com</a>, 2896-2938]<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase"> in man that gives me pause.</span></b>"<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The</b> nestor ["<b>venerable
and wise old man</b>" (dictionary.com)] <b>of Renaissance historians,</b> <b>Jacob
Burckhardt </b>[see 48], was both prophetic and historical, it seems, when he
raised the question in his <i>Reflections on History</i>, "<b>Will
optimism continue to survive and how long?</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Or, as pessimist philosophy of today might seem to suggest, will there
be a general change in thought such as took place in the third and fourth
centuries?"<sup>69</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
answer to his second question that wells up from the demimonde of intellectual
life in our day is a shrill yes.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Jacques [<b>Jack</b>] <b>Kerouac</b>, spokesman for the ragged edge of
the younger set, advertises his contempt for history as being neither true nor
valuable.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Norman Mailer</b> defines
a hipster as "a man who has divorced himself <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">from
history, who does not give a damn about the past."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>On a considerably<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">541<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">higher
level <b>existentialist Sartre cites the reasons why man is not bound by <o:p></o:p></b></span><b><span style="font-family:Arial">history.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For a large
segment of the population, cut off from a serious bond with <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">the
past, whatever value and meaning there is in life is created by the self, while
all outside belongs to the mysterious and impenetrable unpattern[?] of an
unreal reality.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It could be plausibly
argued that a Christian like <b>Cardinal Newman</b> [1801 â€“ 1890] and a pagan
like <b>Seneca</b> [c. 4 B.C.E. â€“ 65 C.E.] had infinitely more in common than a
large part of the postmodern generation (if the reader will forgive the use of
this faddish term) has with either <b>Christianity</b>[<b>newer paganism</b>]
or paganism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is no longer possible
to ignore this loud chorus of "existential screaming," for it is both
symptom and sickness.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>What is, however, more decisive is
the plaintive song of responsible intellectuals, particularly of the younger
men.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Without embarking on a discussion
of the anatomy of revolution and the desertion of the intellectuals, we can at
least suggest that the intellectuals have frequently proved themselves to be
sensitive to great human problems and were their articulate heralds long before
society had followed fateful tendencies toward final consequences.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Only a few examples from the voluminous
"viewing with alarm" literature will have to suffice.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The key word is alienation.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>A brilliant young Harvard-trained
psychologist now at Yale, <b>Kenneth Keniston, spoke out in the Phi Beta Kappa
journal on the problem of Western man:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[Keniston] <b>This is an age that inspires little
enthusiasm.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the industrial West,
and increasingly now in the uncommitted nations of the East, ardor is lacking;
instead men talk of their growing distance from one another, from their social
order, from their work and play, and even from the values that in a perhaps
romanticized past seem to have given their lives cohesiveness and
direction.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Horatio Alger</b> is
replaced by Timon, <b>Napoleon</b> by Ishmael, and even <b>Lincoln</b> now
seems pallid before the defiant images of "hoods" and
"beats."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The vocabulary of
social commentary is dominated by terms that characterize this distance:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>alienation, estrangement, separation,
withdrawal, indifference, disaffection, apathy, noninvolvement, neutralismâ€”all
these words describe the increasing distance between men and their former
objects of love, commitment, loyalty, devotion and reverence.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Alienation, once seen as the consequence of
a cruel (but changeable) economic order, has become for many the central fact
of human existence, characterizing man's "thrown-ness" into a world
in which he has no inherent place.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Formerly
imposed <i>upon</i> men by the world around them, estrangement increasingly is
chosen <i>by</i> them as their dominant reaction to the world.</b><sup>70<o:p></o:p></sup></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><sup><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></sup></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">542<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">The
shift in literature from a preoccupation with the alienation of the outsider,
the member of a minority group, to a concern for the alienation of the common
man as a metaphysical malady is highly indicative.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The American historian and presidential advisor <b>Eric Goldman</b>
once commented sardonically that when the <b>American Negroes</b> have achieved
all their realizable goals, they will discover what the emancipated <b>Jews</b>
learned:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>that life itself is
fundamentally empty [irritating!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>First!, Freedom!, and opportunity].'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[50-51].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Luther spent a lifetime
combating melancholy </b>[how much melancholy, was (and is), due to diet?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>One example:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>goiter.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>How much
melancholy, due to diseases:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>syphilis,
etc.?]<b> and communicating a sense of confidence to his fellowmen.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>There is even a bit of bravado in his
protestations of courage and Christian nonchalance</b>, to borrow <b>Reinhold
Niebuhr</b>'s phrase.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It came to the
surface particularly in crisis situations, as in 1522 when desertions from his
cause were numerous and he [<b>Luther</b>] <b>wrote to Elector Frederick of
Saxony:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[Luther]
<b>Have a little confidence in me, fool though I am</b>, for I know these and
other like tricks of <b>Satan</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I do
not fear him because I know that this hurts him.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Yet all of this is only a beginning.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Let the world cry out and pass its judgments.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Let those fall away who willâ€”even a <b>Saint
Peter</b> or persons like the apostles.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>They will come back on the third day, when <b>Christ </b>rises from the
dead.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This word in II Cor. ch. 6, must
be fulfilled in us:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Let us
approve ourselves in tumults," etc.<sup>81</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Or
again, during the trying days of the Augsburg Diet in 1530, <b>Luther</b> <b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">allegedly</span></b> wrote on the wall in the <b>Koburg</b>
[<b>Castle</b>] the words of the psalm for his own encouragement:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Non moriar sed vivam et narrabo opera
Dei."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He [<b>Luther</b>] <b>found
it necessary to encourage Melanchthon </b>[Philipp Melanchthon (born
Schwartzerd)1497 â€“ 1560]<b> and the less stalwart evangelicals at the Diet:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[Luther] <b>I am displeased with your miserable
worries, with which you write you are consumed and which rule so in your heart.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This shows the magnitude of our unbelief,
not the magnitude of our cause.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For the
same cause was greater in the time of <b>John Hus</b> [1373 â€“ 1415 (reformer,
"burned at the stake")] and many others than it is with us.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But just as the cause is great, so is its
author and initiator, for the cause is not ours.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Therefore, why do you continually and without intermission
weaken?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If the cause is false, let us
renounce it.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If it is true, why do we
make him a <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">liar in such great promises with which he commands us
to be of a calm and quiet mind?<sup>82<o:p></o:p></sup></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">543<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther's correspondence is studded with letters of <i>Seelsorger<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span></i></span></b><span style="font-family:
Arial">[a "physician of souls" (pastor)] <b>combatting depression and
melancholy in men who have turned to him for help.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Luther
sent Matthias Weller a characteristic bit of advice on the problem of his
psychological depression.<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:1.0in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[Luther, to Matthias Weller] <b>Grace and peace in
Christ.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Honorable,
kind, good Friend:<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Your dear brother has informed me
that you are deeply distressed and afflicted with <b>melancholy</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He will undoubtedly tell you what I have
said to him.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Dear Matthias</b>, do not dwell
on your own thoughts, but listen to what other people have to say to you.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For God has commanded men to comfort their
brethren, and it is his will that the afflicted should receive such consolation
as God's very own.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Thus our Lord speaks
through <b>Saint Paul</b>, "Comfort the fainthearted," and through <b>Isaiah</b>:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Comfort ye, comfort ye my people.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Speak ye comfortably."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>And elsewhere our Lord indicated that it is
not his will that man should be downcast, but that he should rather serve the
Lord with gladness and not offer him the sacrifice of sorrow.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>All this <b>Moses</b> and the prophets
declared often and in many places.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Our
Lord also commanded us not to be anxious, but to cast our cares upon him, for
he careth for us, as <b>Saint Peter</b> taught from Ps. 55....<sup>83</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">In
the Table Talk Luther reverted to this theme frequently, as though he perceived
an infectious malady spreading through society.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Especially <b>throughout
the last 15 years of his life</b> he [<b>Luther</b>] <b>warned that solitude
produces melancholy and urged comradeship and social contacts as a cure</b>,
together with playing the lute, prayer, and a host of commonsense devices.<sup>84</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Luther was candid enough to admit that
for all the sound advice he freely dispensed, he found that applying the same
to himself was another matter.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To <b>Conrad
Cordatus</b> he wrote:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"This is in
accord with the saying, 'Good cheer is half the battle,' and, 'A merry heart
doeth good like a medicine:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>but a broken
spirit drieth the bones.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">[luther] <b>I give you this advice although I confess
that I do not take it myself</b></span><b><span style="font-family:Arial">.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<sup>85<o:p></o:p></sup></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><sup><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></sup></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">544<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">That was <b>Luther</b> in another day and another
age, at the end of the Middle Ages, which the medievalist <b>Norman Cantor</b>
has described with the rubric "the life and death of a civilization."<sup>86</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The problem confronting contemporary man may
very well be that of <b>Albrecht DÃ¼rer's</b> [1471 â€“ 1528] <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>W<span style="text-transform:uppercase">ho now will give us certainty</span>?</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">With <b>Erasmus</b>
we too see a certain fatal mutation in human affairs, but <b>need it be fatal?</b><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The audacious survey now happily
completed of man's view of man and his prospects through the long millennia of
Western history at least suggests, if it <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">does
not confirm, certain tentative conclusions.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>A time-line perspective of the problem of man's ambiguous position in
the total scheme of things and of man's ambivalent assessment of that position
suggests that the range of human <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">possibilities
is fortunately limited[?] at the extremes of both pessimism and optimism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The human habitation is provided with both a
floor and a ceiling.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>As <b>Hegel</b>
once reminded his lady friend and future wife, <b>Marie Tucher</b>, "<b>In
all not superficial minds a sense of sadness is linked with all sense of
happiness,</b>" <b>and the reverse is fortunately also usually true.</b><sup>87</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the grand sweep of Western history there
have been periods of decline in which the general mood was depressed and
periods of ascent in which the mood was exuberant.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>But in each period the counterpoint of expectation or despondency
found expression through some articulate spokesman and was recorded for our
contemplation.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>This chiaroscuro
treatment of the human landscape displays broad areas of light and shadow.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But close study of the detail reveals also
that <b>many of the leading figures in pronouncing upon either the grandeur of
man's dignity or the abjectness of his misery have in their own persons given
expression also to the antithetical aspect. </b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp;</span>The picture in terms of broad cultural analysis is complicated in
two ways, then:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>first</b> by the
fact that both motifs were present in varying degrees in at least the major
figures referred to and, <b>second</b>, by the fact that both motifs were found
in varying degrees in all the cultural epochs traversed.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The line runs not merely among men but
through each man, marking off sectors in history of varying areas.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>From within his own historical
perspective <b>man remains a mystery to man</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>It is ironic, in fact, that <b>the world of nature should seem to
be more accessible to human understanding than the world of history</b>, which
man makes and in which he is intimately involved....'<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>[56-58].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>The Political Consequences of the
Reformation</i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, Studies in
Sixteenth-Century Political Thought, by the Rev. <b>R.H. Murray</b>, M.A.,
Litt.D.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Author of </b>"<b>Erasmus
and Luther:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Their Attitude to
Toleration</b>" [see 343], New York, Russell &amp; Russell, 1960 (1926).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>
