<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[<b>dedication</b>]<span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"TO THE<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">VEN. <b>R.H. CHARLES</b>, D.D., D. LITT., LL.D.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">WHO TAUGHTâ€”AND STILL TEACHESâ€”ME TO<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">REALISE THE IMPLICATIONS OF<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">WHAT I KNOW"<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>PREFACE<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">For
over twenty years I have been reading the authors whose writings are analysed
in this book.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I approached them in the first instance
without much criticism and with a receptive mind in order to allow their way of
thinking to permeate my intellect until they became part of the mental
furniture of my mode of thought.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Naturally
I recognised that till I had done so my criticism would not be adequate.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It would of course be wanting in sympathy,
and it would rather tend to defend me against their spirit than enable me to
appreciate it.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In the passing of the
years I have submitted to such seminal thinkers as those dealt with in this
book, and have learned to live in the atmosphere of their ideas to such an
extent that I could almost anticipate the turn of their thoughts on a given
subject.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Then I changed my method, and
stood, as it were, at a considerable distance from my authors in order to be
able to attempt calmly to estimate what their influence on the <b>Reformation</b>
really had been.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To be in contact with
great men and their writings has been the keenest of pleasures, and it will be
a matter of satisfaction to me if I can in any wise convey to the reader some
of my own joy.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The following publishers generously
allowed me to use extracts from books published by them, and I desire to thank
them most cordially:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Macmillan &amp;
Co. (<i>Anglican Essays</i>) and the S.P.C.K. (the Rev. R.H. Murray, <i>Erasmus
and Luther:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Their Attitude to
Toleration</i>).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Mr Laski</b> [apparently, Harold
Joseph Laski 1893 â€“ 1950] read my manuscript with the care and attention that
men seldom bestown upon their own <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">labour.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>My wife</b> gave me the benefit of her
searching criticism.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I thank both of <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">them
most warmly for their criticism no less than for their counsel.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

</span>[ix].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>INTRODUCTION</b><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">THE BACKGROUND OF THE REFORMATION</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[xii]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'The invention of printing gave a
guarantee that the work of the men of the <b>Renaissance</b> would remain, that
the new paths could be trodden now by all, and not, as in mediaeval days, by
the select few.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>True, these paths were
still considered to require supervision.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>For the <b><i>Index Librorum Prohibitorum</i> </b>in England was
established in 1526, thus preceding the first <b><i>Index</i></b><i> </i>on the
Continent by twenty-five years, and that of Rome by thirty-three.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Men like</b> <b>Dr Putnam</b> [see 289,
296] <b>assume that the censorship of books is primarily ecclesiasticalâ€”Papal,
in factâ€”in origin.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Such an
assumption, however, is totally unwarranted.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span></b>As a matter of fact, up to recent times the right of censorship of
printed books was inherent in the State simply because the right to print was a
prerogative of the monarch, be he king, viceroy, archbishop or pope.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>When <b>Charles I.</b> [1600 â€“ 1649; King of
England, Scotland, Ireland, 1625 â€“ 1649 (beheaded)] proclaimed that "<b>the
print is the king's in all countries</b>" he proclaimed the precise truth.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The soil had been ploughed in many
directions, and was ready for any seed that might fall.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Some seed fell by the wayside, in the shape
of the <b><i>Epistolae Obscurorum Virorum</i></b>, that stern survey of the
state of the clergy [laughing!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>My
impression:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>not an accurate statement
regarding the popularity of the <i>Epistolae Obscurorum Virorum</i> (1515 â€“
1517)].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>How much satire undermined the
prestige of Rome is plain to all who turn over the flying sheets of the time.
These satirists realized the sagacity of this expedient.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Their pamphlets circulated on all sides,
creating and moulding public opinion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>They assumed that the corruption of the clergy in general, and the
friars in particular, was a matter known to all.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The <b><i>Ship of Fools </i></b>["a 1494 satire by <b>Sebastian
Brant</b>" (1457 â€“ 1521) (Internet)], for instance, is in reality what <b>Erasmus's
<i>Praise of Folly</i></b> [written 1509, first printed 1511] is only on the
surface.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is a skit on the follies of
mankind, whereas <b>the work</b> [<i>Praise of Folly</i>] <b>of Erasmus is, in
fact, an exposure of the follies and frauds of those who professed to serve the
Church.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For this very reason it must be
counted among the forces preparing for the Reformation.</b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[xii-xiii].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">547<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>In 1511 appeared the</b> <b><i>Encomium
Moriae</i></b> (<b><i>Praise of Folly</i></b>).<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>At a time in which printing was yet in its infancy, the first
edition appeared with no less than eighteen hundred copiesâ€”an enormous issue
for those daysâ€”yet less than a month after the appearance of the book for sale
there were no more than six hundred with the bookseller.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was printed more than seven times in the
course of a few months.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>To the friars
his satire was as the sword of Gideon, and to all his wit was as the spear of
Ithuriel.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Fortunate it was for <b>Erasmus</b>
that <b>Folly</b> [in <i>Praise of Folly</i>] wore such a mask.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The lash of <b>Juvenal</b> or <b>Swift</b>
is forgotten in the mocking smile of <b>Lucian</b> or <b>Voltaire</b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Erasmus satirized follies of all
kinds: </b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>the student for his sickly
look, the grammarian for his self-satisfaction, the philosopher for his
quibbling, the sportsman for his love of butchery, the superstitious for his
belief in the virtues of images and shrines, the sailor for his folly in praying
to the <b>Virgin</b>, and the sinner for his foolishness in believing in the
efficacy of pardons and indulgences.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The king no less than his subjects, the cardinal no less than his
clergy, winced at the scourge of this merry-andrew ["a person who amuses
others by ridiculous behavior" (Internet)].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The main object of Erasmus in
writing the book which dissolved all Europe in laughter was the reform of
religion.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He was, however, wise
enough to know that the more subjects he embraced in his popular writing the more
chance there was of its being read.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>This is evident in the fierceness underlying his ideas.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The credulity of the time moves him to
indignation which is not quite in keeping with the light tone <b>Folly</b>
deigned to assume.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>She might laugh at
those who calculated with mathematical precision the number of years, months
and hours of purgatory, and at those who fondly believed that they could wipe
off a whole life of sin by a small coin.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Folly</b>, all unconscious of her high mission, was lowering the
prestige of the orthodox, thereby preparing the way in no small degree for the
reformer.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">Kings and nobles, cardinals and bishops read the <i>Praise
of Folly</i> with a degree of delight which would have been much diminished had
they grasped its inner significance</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">...."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[xiv].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"....After
1572 the <b>Huguenots</b>, for the most part, had ceased to plead on behalf of
toleration.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Catherine de' Medici</b>
[1519 â€“ 1589] taught them that they must fight if they were to win freedom to
worship God.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">Duplessis-Mornay</span></b> [1549 â€“ 1623 (see 179)], however,
remained true to the political creed of the Politiques, for he ceased not to
urge ably and eloquently the virtues of toleration.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>This quality is present in his <i>Exhortation aux Estates</i>,
which makes a direct appeal to the Roman Catholics to exhibit clemency.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">548<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial">The <b><i>Vindiciae contra Tyrannos</i></b>
["Attributed to <b>Philippe Duplessis Mornay </b>(1549â€“1623) and Hubert
Languet (1518â€“1581)."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>(Internet)]
met with a resounding success.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was
reprinted seven times before <b>1608</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Two English editions appeared during the Civil War and the Revolution,
and were inevitably quoted in Parliament.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Fifteen other works of <span style="text-transform:uppercase">Duplessis-Mornay</span>
were published in England before 1617.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>William Barclay</b> devoted two whole books of his <i>De Regno et
Regalia Potestate adversus Monarchomacos</i>, published in 1600, to a
refutation of the principles of the <i>Vindiciae contra Tyrannos</i>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He is cited, for instance, in a petition to
Parliament in 1593.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Nor does <b>John
Milton</b> disdain to employ a reference to <b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">Mornay</span></b> in his <i>Second Defence of the People of England</i>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Ponet and Harrington, Sidney and Locke
all speak with respect of this French thinker.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Mornay</span>'S influence was not
confined to the Old World.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In
far-distant Connecticut <b>Thomas Hooker</b> quoted the <i>Vindiciae contra
Tyrannos</i>, and <b>John Adams </b>[1735 â€“ 1826 (first Vice President, 1789 â€“
1797; second President, 1797 â€“ 1801)], in his <i>Defence of the Constitution of
the Government of the United States</i>, deemed the pages of the <i>Vindiciae
contra Tyrannos</i> valuable.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">Mornay's</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> <b>concluding
section lifts it out of the dust of the temporal into the serene air of the
eternal.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[209].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">549<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>De Miseria Condicionis Humane </i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">[English and Latin], [<b>Cardinal</b>] <b>Lotario dei
Segni</b> [c. 1161 â€“ 1216] (<b>Pope Innocent III</b> [1198 â€“ 1216]), edited by <b>Robert
E. Lewis</b>, The Chaucer Library, The University of Georgia Press, Athens,
c1978 (<b>1195</b>).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"DATE, AUTHORSHIP, AND CONTENTS<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">OF THE <i>DE MISERIA</i><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Early
in 1195 Cardinal Lotario dei Segni, later Pope Innocent III, wrote a short
treatise that was to become one of the most popular and influential works of
the Middle Agesâ€”the <i>De Miseria Humane Conditionis</i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> (or <i>De Miseria Condicionis Humane</i>, as in the
title of the manuscript used for the text of the present edition).<sup>1</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The treatise is organized into three
parts, called books in the original:</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>the first concerns the wretchedness of man's conception, the disgusting
physical aspects of humans, especially old ones, and the various miseries man
must endure in his life; the second deals with the three goals for which man
strivesâ€”riches, pleasures, and honorsâ€”with exempla and vivid descriptions used
to illustrate the various forms of each; the third concerns the putrefacation
of the body, the pains of hell, and the coming of God on the Day of
Judgment.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The primary source is the
Bible:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>the author either presents an
idea and then quotes a biblical passage or two in support of it or presents the
biblical passage first and then expands on it.</b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>But his learning is not confined to the Bible.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>He also shows a familiarity with the
works of a number of medieval Latin authors, including, among others, Gregory,
Isidore of Seville, Peter Lombard, John of Salisbury, pseudo-St. Bernard, and
Robert of Melun, and even occasionally with the works of such classical authors
as Ovid, Horace, and Juvenal.</b><sup>2</sup><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>...."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[2].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"THE POPULARITY AND INFLUENCE<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">OF THE <i>DE MISERIA<o:p></o:p></i></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">But
whatever the reason for writing it, from the late eleventh century to the
seventeenth century, when the influence of the contemptus mundi idea began to
wane, the <i>De Miseria</i> was the most popular work on the subject, in part
because the author was regarded as one of the greatest of the medieval popes
and in part because <u>it brought together nearly every clichÃ© of earlier works
on contemptus mundi</u>. </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>The popularity of the <i>De Miseria</i> can
be seen in the number of extant manuscripts in which it appears (some 672),<sup>8</sup>
in the number of printed editions it went through by the middle of the
seventeenth <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">550<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">century
(52),<sup>9</sup> and in the number of languages into which it was translated
by the end of the same century (Dutch, English, Flemish, French, German, Irish,
Italian, Spanish).<sup>10</sup><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The popularity of the <i>De
Miseria</i> can also be seen in the enormous extent and variety of its
influence on other writers during the Middle Ages</b>...."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[3].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">Here Begins the Book of the Misery of the
Human Condition Published by Lotario, Cardinal-Deacon of Saints Sergius and
Bachius, Who Was Afterwards Called Pope Innocent the Third.<o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">PREFACE<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="margin-left:.5in;text-align:center;
text-indent:-.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">For
my dearest lord Father Peter, Bishop of Porto and Saint Rufina, Lotario,
unworthy cardinal-deacon, prays for grace in the present and glory in the
future.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;text-transform:uppercase">Here begins the prologue<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">A bit
of leisure, which I caught among many difficulties recently on that occasion
which you know of, did not pass for me completely in leisure, but to put down
pride, which is the chief of all vices, I described the vileness of the human
condition in one way or another.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Nevertheless I have dedicated the title of the present little work to
your name, asking and requesting that if your judgment shall find anything
worthy in it, it ascribe all to divine grace.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Indeed if your reverence shall advise, I will describe, with Christ's
aid, the dignity of human nature, so that just as in this book the haughty man
is humbled, so in the next the humble man may be exalted.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[HERE BEGINS THE FIRST PART]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[1] <span style="text-transform:uppercase">of the
misery of man<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"Why
came I out of my mother's womb to see labor and sorrow and that my days should
be spent in confusion?"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If he whom
God sanctified in the womb spoke such things about himself, what things shall I
say of myself, whom my mother brought forth in sin?<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Ah me, I might say, my mother, why did you bear me, the son of
bitterness and sorrow?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Why did I
not die in the womb?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Having come out of
the belly, why did I not perish at once?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Why received upon the knees, suckled <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">551<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">at
the breasts," born "for burning and for fuel for the fire"?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If only I had been destroyed in the womb, so
"that my mother might have been my grave and her womb an everlasting
conception."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"For I should
have been as if I had not been, carried from the womb to the grave."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Who therefore will give my eyes a fountain
of tears so that I may bewail the miserable beginning of the human condition,
the culpable progress of human behavior, the damnable ending of human dissoluteness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>With tears I might consider what man is made
of, what man does, what man will be.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>Man is indeed formed from earth, conceived in sin, born to pain.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He does depraved things that are unlawful,
shameful things that are indecent, vain things that are unprofitable.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He becomes fuel for the fire, food for
worms, a mass of putridness.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>I shall
show this more clearly; I shall analyze more fully.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Man is formed of dust, of clay, of ashes:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>what is more vile, from the filthiest
sperm.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He is conceived in the heat of
desire, in the fervor of the flesh, in the stench of lust:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>what is worse, in the blemish of sin.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He is born to labor, fear, sorrow:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>what is more miserable, to death.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He does depraved things by which he offends
God, offends his neighbors, offends himself.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>He does vain and shameful things by which he pollutes his fame, pollutes
his person, pollutes his conscience.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He
does vain things by which he neglects serious things, neglects profitable
things, neglects necessary things.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He
will become fuel for the inextinguishable fire that always flames and burns;
food for the immortal worm that always eats and consumes; a mass of horrible
putridness that always stinks and is filthy.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[92, 94].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'THE THIRD PART<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">[1] OF THE ROTTENNESS OF CORPSES<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"His
spirit shall go forth, and he shall return into his earth; in that day all
their thoughts shall perish."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>O
how many and how great the things mortals plan on account of the uncertainty of
worldly foreknowledge, but at the moment of sudden death the things that they
had planned suddenly disappear.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"I
am taken away like the shadow when it declineth, and I am shaken off as
locusts."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Therefore the spirit
does not go forth willing, but unwilling, because it gives up with sorrow what
it possessed with love, and whether it wishes or not, a limit has been set for
it that cannot be gone beyond, at which earth shall return to earth.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For it is written:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>"Earth thou art, and into earth thou shalt
return."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Certainly it is natural
that something made of matter should be dissolved into matter.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"He shall therefore take away their
breath, and they shall fail, and shall return to their dust."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But when man shall die, he shall inherit
beasts, serpents, and worms.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"For
they shall all sleep in the dust, and worms shall cover them."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"For the worm shall eat them up as a
garment, and the moth shall consume them as wool."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"I am to be consumed as rottenness and
as a garment that is moth-eaten."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"I have said to <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">552<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">rottenness,
'Thou art my father'; to worms, 'my mother and my sister'."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Man is<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>rottenness, and his son a worm."<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>How foul the father, how vile the mother, how abominable the
sister!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For man is conceived of blood
made rotten by the fire of lust; in the end worms stand by his body like
mourners.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Alive, he brings forth lice
and tapeworms; dead, he will beget worms and flies.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>Alive, he produces dung and vomit; dead, he produces rottenness
and stench.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Alive, he fattens one man;
dead, he will fatten many worms.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What,
then, is more foul smelling than a human corpse?<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>What more horrible than a dead man?<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>He whose embrace was most pleasing in life will indeed be a
disgusting sight in death.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What good,
therefore, are riches?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What good
sumptuous food?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>What good
delicacies?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>They will not free from
death, will not defend from the worm, will not take away from the stench.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>He who was lately sitting glorious on the
throne now lies despised in the grave; he who was lately shining splendid in
the palace is now slighted naked in the tomb; he who was lately filling himself
with delicacies in the dining hall is now consumed by worms in the
sepulcher.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[204, 206].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

of other cheerful reading</b>]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"[14]<span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>OF THE POWER, WISDOM, AND JUSTICE OF THE
JUDGE"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[226]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:right 27.0pt"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:right 27.0pt"><span style="font-family:
Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1"> </span>"[15]<span style="mso-tab-count:
1">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>OF DIVINE JUDGMENT"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[230]<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:right 27.0pt"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:right 27.0pt"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:right 27.0pt"><span style="font-family:Arial">'[16] THAT NOTHING SHALL BENEFIT THE DAMNED<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">Then
riches will not benefit, nor honors protect, nor friends support.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>For it is written:<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>"Their silver and gold shall not be able to deliver them in
the day of the wrath of the Lord."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>"The kings of the earth shall weep and wail when they see the smoke
of the burning," "for fear of its torments."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"What therefore will ye do in the day
of visitation and calamity which cometh from afar?<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>To whom will ye flee for help?"<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>"Everyone shall bear his own burden."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"The soul that sins, the same shall
die."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>O severe judgment, in which
not only of deeds, but "of every idle word that men have spoken, they
shall render an account," in which the debt will be exacted with interest
up to the last farthing.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Who
therefore will be able to flee from the wrath to come?"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"Therefore the Son of Man shall send
his angels, and they shall gather out of his kingdom all scandals and them that
work iniquity"; they shall bind them in bundles for burning "and
shall cast them into the furnace of glowing fire.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>There shall be weeping" and moaning, wailing and shrieking,
grief and torment, gnashing and shouting, fear and trembling, labor and pain,
fire and stench, darkness and anxiety, anguish and harshness, calamity and
want, distress and sorrow, oblivion and confusion, tortures and pains,
bitternesses and terrors, hunger and thirst, cold and heat, brimstone and fire
burning forever and ever.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">Here
Ends the Book of the Misery of the Human Condition Published by Lotario,
Cardinal-Deacon of Saints Sergius and Bachius, Who Was Afterwards Called Pope
Innocent the Third.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">' <span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;</span>[230, 232].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:
Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">554<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>A History of Modern Culture</i>, by
Preserved Smith</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, Hon. Litt.D.
Amherst, Professor of History in Cornell University, <b>Volume II</b> [of two
volumes], <b>The Enlightenment, 1687â€“1776</b>, published by Peter Smith, 1957
(c1934) (Volume 1, c1930).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'The Christian apologist <b>Warburton</b> represents
the ancient mysteries as established by the state for the peace of civil
society.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Holbach </b>[1723 â€“ 1789]<b>,
the atheist, declared:<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">If we go back to the beginning we shall always
find that ignorance and fear have created the gods; fancy, enthusiasm, or
deceit has adorned or disfigured them; weakness worships them; credulity keeps
them alive; custom imposes regard for them; and tyranny supports them in order
to use the blindness of men for its own ends.<o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The
most elaborate exposition of this doctrine of the artificial creation of
religions for secular purposes is found in the <b><i>Testament</i> of Jean
Meslier </b>[1664 â€“ 1729]<b> </b>published, twenty-nine years after the
author's death, by <b>Voltaire </b>[1694 â€“ 1778].<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Meslier</b> <b>was a French curate</b> who was turned into a
bitter enemy of religion by seeing it used, by unbelieving princes and
prelates, as an instrument to oppress the poor.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Not daring to print his thoughts openly, he left them to
posterity in a manuscript</b>, which he called his <i>Will</i>, or, more fully,<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="margin-left:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></i><span style="font-family:Arial">[<b>Meslier</b>] <i>Thoughts and Sentiments on some
of the abuses and errors in the guidance and government of men, by which the
vanity and falsity of all the religions of the world are clearly and
conclusively demonstrated</i>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial">The sufferings and oppression of men he believed due
to the "detestable policy of those wishing to rule over their fellows
unjustly, or else ambitious of a reputation for holiness or even for
divinity."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;text-transform:uppercase">Religion is nothing but</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> "<b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">abuse,
error, illusion, falsehood and imposture</span></b>, <o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">calculated to make human laws pass for divine laws.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
miracles, the mysteries, the morals of Christianity are subjected to a
withering analysis, and this is followed by an attack on theism and a
profession of materialism.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[521].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in center 3.0in right 6.0in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Wingdings;mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:
Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:Arial;mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:
Wingdings"><span style="mso-char-type:symbol;mso-symbol-font-family:Wingdings">l</span></span><span style="font-family:Arial"> </span><span style="font-family:Wingdings;
mso-ascii-font-family:Arial;mso-hansi-font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-family:

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">555<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Jesus Son of Man</i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">, Preface by <b>Gore Vidal</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Afterword by <b>David Noel Freedman</b>,
translated by <b>Hugh Young</b>, <b>Rudolf Augstein </b>[1923 â€“ 2002 (founded <i>Der
Spiegel</i>, 1946/1947)], Urizen Books, 1977 (1972 German).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>Preface<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">by Gore Vidal<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Whether or not <b>Jesus</b> actually
resembles the mysterious and contradictory figure described in the <b>Gospels</b>
(Greek for "good news") is unknowable and unimportant.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">In fact, it is quite possible that Jesus never
existed in history.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">On
the other hand, there is no doubt that the life of the West for nearly two
millennia has been dominated by <b>Christianity, that protean yet always somber
creed which has not only served beautifully the princes of this world but also
afforded occasional solace to those made wretched by their anointed lords</b>...."<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[7].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">"<b>10.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;text-transform:uppercase">Mark, a disappointing
witness<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial;text-transform:uppercase">Conversation in the year 33<o:p></o:p></span></i></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></i></b></p>
