<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">557<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">from:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Curiosities of Literature</i></span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>By <b>Isaac
Disraeli </b>[1766 â€“ 1848].<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Vol. III</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>1858 (<b>1791</b>).<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>Leo X.</b> projected an alliance
of the sovereigns of <b>Christendom</b> against the <b>Turks</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The avowed object was to oppose the progress
of the Ottomans against the Mamelukes of Egypt, who were more friendly to the <b>Christians</b>;
but <b>the concealed motive with</b> his holiness [<b>Leo </b>X] <b>was to
enrich himself and his family with the spoils of</b> <b>Christendom</b>, and to
aggrandize the papal throne by war; and such, indeed, the policy of these
pontiffs had always been in those mad crusades which they excited against the
East.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>The Reformation,</b> excellent as
its results have proved in the cause of genuine freedom, <b>originated in no
purer source than human passions and selfish motives:</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>it was the progeny of avarice in Germany, of
novelty in France, and of love in England.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>The latter is elegantly alluded to by <b>Gray </b>[Gay?]â€”<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">And gospel-light first beam'd from Bullen's eyes.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">The <b>Reformation</b>
is considered by the <b>Duke of Nevers</b>, in a work printed in 1590, as it
had been by <b>Francis I.</b>, in his Apology in 1537, as a <i>coup-d' Ã©tat</i>
of <b>Charles V.</b> towards universal monarchy.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The duke says, that the emperor silently permitted <b>Luther</b>
to establish his principles in Germany, that they might split the confederacy
of the elective princes, and by this division facilitate their more easy
conquest, and play them off one against another, and by these means to secure
the imperial crown hereditary in the house of Austria.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Had <b>Charles V.</b> not been the mere
creature of his politics, and had he felt any zeal for the Catholic cause,
which he pretended to fight for, never would he have allowed the new doctrines
to spread for more than twenty years without the least opposition....'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[142].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'"<b>POLITICAL RELIGIONISM.</b>"<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">In
Professor <b>Dugald Stewart</b>'s first Dissertation on the Progress of
Philosophy, I find this singular and significant term.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">It
has occasioned me to reflect on those contests for religion, in which a
particular faith has been made the ostensible pretext, while the secret motive
was usually political.</span></b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The
historians, who view in religious wars only religion itself, have written large
volumes, in which we may never discover that they have either been a struggle to
obtain predominance, or an expedient to secure it.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b><span style="text-transform:uppercase">The hatreds of
ambitious men have disguised their own purposes, while Christianity has borne <o:p></o:p></span></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">558<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">the odium of loosening a destroying spirit among
mankind; <o:p></o:p></span></b><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
text-transform:uppercase">which, had Christianity never existed, would have
equally prevailed in human affairs.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Of a moral malady, it is not only necessary
to know the nature, but to designate it by a right name, that we may not err in
our mode of treatment.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>If we call that <i>religious</i>
which we shall find for the greater part is <i>political</i>, we are likely to
be mistaken in the regimen and the cure.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[238-239].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b><span style="text-transform:
uppercase">Whether the reformed were martyred by the catholics, or the
catholics executed by the reformed; whether the puritans expelled those of the
established church, or the established church ejected the puritans, all seems
reducible to two classes, conformists and non-conformists, or, in the political
style, the administration and the opposition.</span></b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>When we discover that the heads of all
parties are of the same hot temperament, and observe the same evil conduct in
similar situations; when we view honest old <b>Latimer</b> with his own hands
hanging a mendicant friar on a tree, and, the government changing, the friars
binding <b>Latimer</b> to the stake; when we see the French catholics cutting
out the tongues of the protestants, that they might no longer protest; the
haughty Luther writing submissive apologies to <b>Leo the Tenth</b> and <b>Henry
the Eighth</b> for the scurrility with which he had treated them in his
writings, and finding that his apologies were received with contempt, then
retracting his retractions; when we find that haughtiest of the haughty, <b>John
Knox</b>, when <b>Elizabeth</b> first ascended the throne, crouching and
repenting of having written his famous excommunication against all female
sovereignty; or pulling down the monasteries, from the axiom that when the
rookery was destroyed, the rooks would never return; when we find his recent
apologist admiring, while he apologizes for, some extraordinary proofs of
Machiavelian politics, an impenetrable mystery seems to hang over the conduct
of men who profess to be guided by the bloodless code of <b>Jesus</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>But try them by a human standard, and treat
them as <i>politicians</i>, and the motives once discovered, the actions are
understood!<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Two edicts of Charles the Fifth,
in 1555, condemned to death the Reformed of the Low Countries, even should they
return to the catholic faith, with this exception, however, in favour of the
latter, that they shall not be burnt alive, but that the men shall be beheaded,
and the women buried alive!</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><i>Religion</i>
could not, then, be the real motive of the Spanish cabinet, for in returning to
the ancient faith that point was obtained; but the truth is, that the Spanish
government considered the reformed as <i>rebels</i>, whom it was not safe to
re-admit to the rights of citizenship.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>The
undisguised fact appears in the codicil to the will of the emperor, when he
solemnly declares that he had written to the Inquisition </b>"<b>to burn
and extirpate the heretics,</b>"<b> <i>after trying to <o:p></o:p></i></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">559<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><i><span style="font-family:Arial">make
Christians of them</span></i></b><b><span style="font-family:Arial">, because
he is convinced that they never can <o:p></o:p></span></b><b><span style="font-family:Arial">become
sincere catholics</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">; and he
acknowledges that he had committed a great fault in permitting <b>Luther</b> to
return free on the faith of his safe-conduct, as <b>the emperor was not bound
to keep a promise with a heretic. </b><span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp;</span>"<b>It is because that I destroyed him not, that heresy has
now become strong, which I am convinced might have been stifled with him in its
birth.</b>"<b>*</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[see footnote,
below]<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The whole conduct of <b>Charles
the Fifth</b> in this mighty revolution was, from its beginning, censured by
contemporaries as purely <i>political</i>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Francis the First</b> observed that the emperor, under the colour of
religion, was placing himself at the head of a league to make his way to a
predominant monarchy.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"The pretext
of religion is no new thing," writes the <b>Duke of Nevers</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>"<b>Charles the Fifth</b> had never
undertaken a war against the Protestant princes but with the design of
rendering the Imperial crown hereditary in the house of Austria; and he has
only attacked the electoral princes to ruin them, and to abolish their right of
election.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Had it been zeal for the
catholic religion, would he have delayed from 1519 to 1549 to arm?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>That he might have extinguished the
Lutheran heresy, which he could easily have done in 1526, but he considered
that this novelty would serve to divide the German princes, and he patiently
waited till the effect was realized.</b>"<b>â€ </b>'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[242-243].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>[<b>footnotes</b>] '<b>*Llorente's </b>"<b>Critical
History of the Inquisition.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">â€ </span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> NaudÃ©, "ConsidÃ©rations Politiques," p.
115.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>See a curious note in Hart's
"Life of Gustavus Adolphus," ii. 129.'<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>[243].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>This subject of "Political
Religionism" is indeed as nice as it is curious; <i>politics</i> have been
so cunningly worked into the cause of <i>religion</i>, that the parties
themselves will never be able to separate them</b>; and to this moment the most
opposite opinions are formed concerning the same events and the same
persons.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[244].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>TOLERATION.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">An
enlightened toleration is a blessing of the last ageâ€”it would seem to have been
practiced by the Romans, when they did not mistake the primitive <b>Christians</b>
for seditious members of society; and was inculcated even by <b>Mahomet</b>, in
a passage in the <b>Koran</b>, but scarcely practiced by his followers.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>In modern history it was condemned when
religion was turned into a political contest under the aspiring house of
Austriaâ€”and in Spainâ€”and in France.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It
required a long time before its nature was comprehendedâ€”and to this moment it
is far from being clear, either to the tolerators or the tolerated.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">560<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b><span style="font-family:Arial">It does not appear that the precepts or the practice
of Jesus and the apostles inculcate the <i>compelling</i> of any to be</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial"> <b>Christians;</b>* <b>yet</b> an expression
employed in the nuptial parable of the great supper, when the hospitable lord
commanded the servant, finding that he had still room to accommodate more
guests, to go out in the highways and hedges, and "<b><i>compel them to
come in, that my house may be filled</i>,</b>" <b>was alleged as an
authority by those catholics who called themselves </b>"<b>the converters,</b>"
<b>for using religious force, which, still alluding to the hospitable lord,
they called </b>"<b>a charitable and salutary violence.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It was this circumstance which produced <b>Bayle</b>'s
"Commentaire Philosophique sur ces Paroles de <b>Jesus Christ</b>,"
published under the supposititious [spurious] name of an <i>Englishman</i>, as
printed at Canterbury in 1686, but really at Amsterdam.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is curious that <b>Locke</b> published
his first letter on "<b>Toleration</b>" in Latin at Gouda, in
1689â€”the second in 1690â€”and the third in 1692.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span><b>Bayle</b> opened the mind of <b>Locke</b>, and some time after quotes
<b>Locke</b>'s Latin letter with high commendation.â€ <span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>The caution of both writers in publishing in foreign places,
however, indicates the prudence which it was deemed necessary to observe in
writing in favour of toleration.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>[245].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'<b>THE PEARL BIBLES AND SIX THOUSAND ERRATA.<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">As
a literary curiosity, I notice a subject which might rather enter into the
history of religion.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It relates to the
extraordinary state of our English Bibles, which were for some time suffered to
be so corrupted that no books ever yet swarmed with such innumerable errata!<o:p></o:p></span></b></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b><u>These errata </u></b><u>[errors
in printing]<b> unquestionably were in great part voluntary commissions,
passages interpolated, and meanings forged for certain purposes</b></u><b>;
sometimes to sanction the new creed of a half-hatched sect, and sometimes with
an intention to destroy all scriptural authority by a confusion, or an omission
of textsâ€”the whole was left open to the option or the malignity of the editors,
who, probably, like certain ingenious wine-merchants, contrived to accommodate
"the waters of life" to their customers' peculiar taste.</b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>They had also a project of printing Bibles
as cheaply and in a form as contracted as they possibly could for the common
people; and they proceeded till it nearly ended with having no Bible at all:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>and, as <b>Fuller</b>, in his "Mixt
Contemplations on Better Times," alluding to this circumstance, with not
one of his lucky quibbles, observes, "The <i>small price </i>of the Bible
has caused the <i>small prizing</i> of the Bible."'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[427-428].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">561<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">'....Another
competition arose among those who printed <b>English Bibles in Holland</b>, in <i>duodecimo</i>,
with an English colophon, for half the price even of the <o:p></o:p></span><span style="font-family:Arial">lowest
in London.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Twelve thousand of these <i>duodecimo</i>
Bibles, with notes, fabricated in Holland, usually by our fugitive sectarians,
were seized by the king's printers, as contrary to the statute.*<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Such was this shameful war of biblesâ€”folios,
quartos, and duodecimos, even in the days of <b>Charles the First</b>.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>The public spirit of the rising sects was
the real occasion of these increased demands for Bibles.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>During the civil wars they carried
on the same open trade and competition, besides the private ventures of the
smuggled Bibles.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>A large impression
of these Dutch English Bibles were burnt by order of the Assembly of Divines,
for these <i>three errors:</i>â€”<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Gen. xxxvi. 24.â€”This is that <b><i>ass</i></b>
that found rulers in the wildernessâ€”<b>for <i>mule</i></b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Ruth iv. 13.â€”"The Lord gave her
<b><i>corruption</i></b>â€”<b>for <i>conception</i></b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Luke xxi. 28.â€”Look up, and lift up
your hands, for your <b><i>condemnation </i></b>draweth nighâ€”<b>for <i>redemption</i></b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>These errata were none [?] of the
printer's; but, as a writer of the times expresses it, "<b>egregious
blasphemies, and damnable errata</b>" <b>of some sectarian</b>, or some
Bellamy [Edward Bellamy?<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>(1850 â€“ 1898)]
<b>editor of that day!<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>The printing of Bibles at length was
a privilege conceded to one <b>William Bentley</b>; but he was opposed by <b>Hills
and Field</b>; and a paper war arose, in which they mutually recriminated on
each other, with equal truth.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Field printed, in 1653, what was
called the Pearl Bible</b>; alluding, I suppose, to that diminutive type in
printing, for it could not derive its name from its worth.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>It is in twenty-fours;<b>*</b> [see
footnote, 564] but to contract the mighty book into this dwarfishness, all the
original Hebrew text prefixed to the Psalms, explaining the occasion and the
subject of their composition, is wholly expunged.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span><b>This Pearl Bible, which may be inspected among the great
collection of our English Bibles at the British Museum, is set off by many <u>notable
<i>errata</i></u>, of which these are noticed:â€”<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>Romans vi. 13.</b>â€”Neither yield

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b><span style="font-family:Arial">First Corinthians vi. 9.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">â€”Know ye not that the unrighteous <b><i>shall inherit</i>
</b>the kingdom of God?â€”<b>for <i>shall not inherit</i></b>.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>This <i>erratum</i> ["error in
printing"] served as the foundation of a dangerous doctrine; for many
libertines urged the text from this corrupt Bible against the reproofs of a divine.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>This <b><u>Field was a great forger</u>
</b>[see christianism.com, 1735-1899]<b>; and it is said that he received a
present of 1500<i>l</i>. from the <i>Independents</i> to corrupt a text in Acts
vi. 3, to sanction the right of the people to appoint their own pastors.â€ </b>
[see footnote, 564] <b>The corruption was the easiest possible; it was only to
be put a <i>ye</i> instead of a <i>we;</i> so that the right in Field's Bible
emanated from the people, not from the apostles.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span></b>The only account I recollect of this extraordinary state of
our Bibles is a happy allusion in a line of <b>Butler:â€”<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Religion
spawn'd a various rout,<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Of
petulant, capricious sects,<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>THE
MAGGOTS OF CORRUPTED TEXTS.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="text-indent:.5in;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><b><span style="font-family:Arial">In
other Bibles by Hills and Field we may find such abundant errata, reducing the
text to nonsense or to blasphemy</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial">,
making the Scriptures contemptible to the multitude, who came to pray, and not
to scoff.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>It is affirmed, in the manuscript
account already referred to, that one Bible swarmed with <i>six thousand
faults!</i></b><span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>Indeed, from another
source we discover that "<b>Sterne, a solid scholar, was the first who
summed up the <i>three thousand and six hundred </i>faults<span style="mso-bidi-font-style:italic"> that were in our printed Bibles of London.</span></b><span style="mso-bidi-font-style:italic">"*<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>If one book can be made to contain near four thousand errors, like
ingenuity was required to reach to six thousand; but perhaps this is the first
time so remarkable an incident in the history of literature has ever been
chronicled.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>And that famous edition of
the <b>Vulgate</b>, by <b>Pope Sixtus the Fifth </b>[Pope 1585 â€“ 1590 (1520 â€“
1590)], a memorable book of blunders, which commands such high prices, ought
now to fall in value, before the pearl Bible, in twenty-fours, of <b>Messrs.
Hills and Field</b>!'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[429-431].<o:p></o:p></span></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;
mso-bidi-font-style:italic"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;
mso-bidi-font-style:italic"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">563<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" align="center" style="text-align:center;tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial">________________________________________________________________<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<span style="font-size:12.0pt;font-family:Arial;mso-fareast-font-family:&quot;Times New Roman&quot;;
mso-ansi-language:EN-US;mso-fareast-language:EN-US;mso-bidi-language:AR-SA"><br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always">
</span>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span style="font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-style:italic">[<b>footnotes </b>(from
562, 563)] '<b>*</b>A technical printing-term for a sheet containing
twenty-four pages.<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;
mso-bidi-font-style:italic"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial;
mso-bidi-font-style:italic"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><b>â€ </b>The
passage is as follows, and is addressed by the apostles to "the multitude
of the disciples," who desired an improved clerical rule:â€”"<b>Wherefore,
brethren, look yet out among you seven men of honest report, full of the Holy
Ghost and wisdom, whom </b></span><b><i style="mso-bidi-font-style:normal"><span style="font-family:Arial">we</span></i></b><b><span style="font-family:Arial;
mso-bidi-font-style:italic"> may appoint over this business.</span></b><span style="font-family:Arial;mso-bidi-font-style:italic">"'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[430].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><!--[if !supportEmptyParas]-->&nbsp;<!--[endif]--><o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:.5in"><span style="font-family:Arial"><span style="mso-tab-count:1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>'<b>The proverbial expression of <i>chapter
and verse</i> seems peculiar to ourselves, and, I suspect, originated in the
puritanic period, probably just before the civil wars under Charles the First,
from the frequent use of appealing to the Bible on the most frivolous
occasions, practiced by those whom South calls </b>"<b>those mighty men at
<i>chapter and verse</i>.</b>"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>With a sort of religious coquetry, they were vain of perpetually opening
their gilt pocket Bibles; they perked them up with such self-sufficiency and
perfect ignorance of the original, that the learned <b>Selden</b> found
considerable amusement in going to their "assembly of divines," and
puzzling or confuting them, as we have noticed.<span style="mso-spacerun:
yes">&nbsp; </span>A ludicrous anecdote on one of these occasions is given by a
contemporary, which shows how admirably that learned man amused himself with
this "assembly of divines!"<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp;
</span>They were discussing the distance between Jerusalem and Jericho, with a
perfect ignorance of sacred or of ancient geography; one said it was twenty
miles, another ten, and at last it was concluded to be only seven, for this
strange reason, that fish was brought from Jericho to Jerusalem market!<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span><b>Selden</b> observed, that "possibly
the fish in question was salted," and silenced these acute
disputants.'<span style="mso-spacerun: yes">&nbsp; </span>[432].<o:p></o:p></span></p>

<p class="MsoFooter" style="tab-stops:right 5.75in"><span style="font-family:
